GENERAL PROVISIONS
§ 10.01 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this code of ordinances, the following definitions shall
apply unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   CITY. The City of Malta, Montana, or the area within the territorial limits
of the City of Malta, Montana, and such territory outside of the City of Malta
over which the city has jurisdiction or control by virtue of any constitutional
or statutory provision.
   COUNCIL. The City Council of the city. ALL ITS MEMBERS or ALL COUNCIL
MEMBERS means the total number of Council members holding office.
   COUNTY. The County of Phillips, State of Montana.
   LAW. Applicable federal law, the Constitution and statutes of the State of
Montana, the ordinances of the city and, when appropriate, any and all rules
and regulations which may be promulgated thereunder.
   MAY. The act referred to is permissive.
   MONTH. A calendar month.
   MUST and SHALL. The acts referred to are each mandatory.
   OATH. Includes an affirmation or declaration in all cases in which, by law,
an affirmation may be substituted for an oath and, in such cases, the words
“swear” and “sworn” shall be equivalent to the words “affirm” and “affirmed”.
   OWNER. Applied to a building or land, includes any part owner, joint owner,
tenant in common, joint tenant, tenant by the entirety of the whole or a part
of such building or land.
   PERSON. Includes a natural person, joint venture, joint stock company,
partnership, association, club, company, corporation, business, trust,
organization or the manager, lessee, agent, servant, officer or employee of any
of them.
   PERSONAL PROPERTY. Includes money, goods, chattels, things in action and
evidences of debt.
   PRECEDING and FOLLOWING. Next before and next after, respectively.
   PROPERTY. Includes real and personal property.
   REAL PROPERTY. Includes land, tenements and hereditaments.
   SIDEWALK. The portion of a street between the curbline and the adjacent
property line intended for the use of pedestrians.
   STATE. The State of Montana.
   STREET. Includes all streets, highways, avenues, lanes, alleys, courts,
places, squares, curbs or other public ways in the city which have been or may
hereafter be dedicated and open to the public use or such other public property
so designated in any law of the state.
   TENANT and OCCUPANT. Applied to a building or land, include any person who
occupies the whole or part of such building or land, whether alone or with
others.
   WRITTEN. Includes printed, typewritten, mimeographed, multigraphed or
otherwise reproduced in permanent visible form.
   YEAR. A calendar year.
(Prior Code, § 1.04.010) (Ord. 306, passed - -1979)
§ 10.02 TITLE OF OFFICE.
   Use of the title of any officer, employee, department, board or commission
means that officer, employee, department, board or commission of the city.
(Prior Code, § 1.04.020) (Ord. 306, passed - -1979)
§ 10.03 INTERPRETATION OF LANGUAGE.
   All words and phrases shall be construed according to the common and
approved usage of the language, but technical words and phrases and such others
as may have acquired a peculiar and appropriate meaning in the law shall be
construed and understood according to such peculiar and appropriate meaning.
(Prior Code, § 1.04.030) (Ord. 306, passed - -1979)
§ 10.04 GRAMMATICAL INTERPRETATION.
   The following grammatical rules shall apply in the ordinances of the city,
unless it is apparent from the context that a different construction is
intended.
   (A)   Gender. Each gender includes the masculine, feminine and neuter
genders.
   (B)   Singular and plural. The singular number includes the plural and the
plural includes the singular.
   (C)   Tenses. Words used in the present tense include the past and the
future tenses and vise versa, unless manifestly inapplicable.
(Prior Code, § 1.04.040) (Ord. 306, passed - -1979)
§ 10.05 ACTS BY AGENTS.
   When an act is required by an ordinance, the same being such that it may be
done as well by an agent as by the principal, such requirement shall be
construed to include all such acts performed by an authorized agent.
(Prior Code, § 1.04.050) (Ord. 306, passed - -1979)
§ 10.06 PROHIBITED ACTS INCLUDE CAUSING AND PERMITTING.
   Whenever in the ordinances of the city, any act of omission is made
unlawful, it shall include causing, allowing, permitting, aiding, abetting,
suffering or concealing the fact of such act or omission.
(Prior Code, § 1.04.060) (Ord. 306, passed - -1979)
§ 10.07 COMPUTATION OF TIME.
   Except when otherwise provided, the time within which an act is required to
be done shall be computed by excluding the first day and including the last
day, unless the last day is Sunday or a holiday, in which case it shall also be
excluded.
(Prior Code, § 1.04.070) (Ord. 306, passed - -1979)
§ 10.08 CONSTRUCTION.
   The provisions of the ordinances of the city, and all proceedings under
them, are to be construed with a view to effect their objects and to promote
justice.
(Prior Code, § 1.04.080) (Ord. 306, passed - -1979)
§ 10.09 REPEAL SHALL NOT REVIVE ANY ORDINANCES.
   The repeal of an ordinance shall not repeal the repealing clause of an
ordinance or revive any ordinance which has been repealed thereby.
(Prior Code, § 1.04.090) (Ord. 306, passed - -1979)
CODE ADOPTION
§ 10.20 ADOPTION.
   There is adopted the “Malta Municipal Code”, as published by American Legal
Publishing Corporation.
(Prior Code, § 1.01.010) (Ord. 319, passed - -1980)
§ 10.21 TITLE; CITATION; REFERENCE.
   This code shall be known as the “Malta Municipal Code” and it shall be
referred to as the “Malta Municipal Code” or “this code” or “this code of
ordinances” in any prosecution for the violation of any provisions thereof or
in any proceeding at law or equity. Prosecutions for violations of city’s
ordinances and actions based thereon shall refer to the municipal code
sections. Amendments to any ordinance or portions thereof of the city shall
also refer to the municipal code sections under which such ordinances are
codified.
(Prior Code, § 1.01.020) (Ord. 319, passed - -1980)
§ 10.22 PROVISIONS CODIFIED.
   This code consists of all the regulatory, general and penal ordinances and
certain of the administrative ordinances of the city.
(Prior Code, § 1.01.030) (Ord. 319, passed - -1980)
§ 10.23 REFERENCE APPLIES TO ALL AMENDMENTS.
   Whenever a reference is made to this code as the “Malta Municipal Code”, or
to any portion thereof, or to any ordinances of the city, the reference shall
apply to all amendments, corrections and additions heretofore, now or hereafter
made.
(Prior Code, § 1.01.040) (Ord. 319, passed - -1980)
§ 10.24 TITLE, CHAPTER AND SECTION HEADINGS.
   Title, chapter and section headings contained in this code shall not be
deemed to govern, limit, modify or in any manner affect the scope, meaning or
intent of the provisions of any title, chapter or section hereof.
(Prior Code, § 1.01.050) (Ord. 319, passed - -1980)
§ 10.25 REFERENCE TO SPECIFIC ORDINANCES.
   A provision of this code shall not in any manner affect matters of record
which refer to, or are otherwise connected with ordinances which are
specifically designated by number or otherwise and which are included within
the code, but such reference shall be construed to apply to the corresponding
provisions contained within this code.
(Prior Code, § 1.01.060) (Ord. 319, passed - -1980)
§ 10.26 EFFECT OF CODE ON PAST ACTIONS AND OBLIGATIONS.
   Neither the adoption of this code, nor the repeal or amendment of any
ordinance or portion of any ordinance of the city, shall in any manner affect
the prosecution for violations of ordinances, which violations were committed
prior to the effective date hereof, nor be construed as a waiver of any
license, fee or penalty at said effective date due and unpaid under any such
ordinances, nor be construed as affecting any of the provisions of such
ordinances relating to the collection of any such license, fee or penalty or
the penal provisions applicable to any violation thereof, nor to affect the
validity of any bond or cash deposit in lieu thereof required to be posted,
filed or deposited pursuant to any ordinance and all rights and obligations
thereunder appertaining shall continue in full force and effect.
(Prior Code, § 1.01.070) (Ord. 319, passed - -1980)
§ 10.27 EFFECTIVE DATE.
   This code shall become effective on the date the ordinance adopting this
code as the “Malta Municipal Code” shall become effective.
(Prior Code, § 1.01.080) (Ord. 319, passed - -1980)
§ 10.28 CONSTITUTIONALITY.
   (A)   If any section, division, sentence, clause or phrase of this code is
for any reason held to be invalid or unconstitutional, such holding shall not
affect the validity of the remaining portions of this code.
   (B)   The City Council declares that it would have passed this code and each
section, division, sentence, clause and phrase thereof irrespective of the fact
that any one or more sections, divisions, sentences, clauses or phrases had
been declared invalid or unconstitutional and if, for any reason, this code
shall be declared invalid or unconstitutional, then the original ordinance or
ordinances shall be in full force and effect.
(Prior Code, § 1.01.090) (Ord. 319, passed - -1980)
§ 10.29 ORDINANCES UNAFFECTED.
   All ordinances of a temporary or special nature, and all other ordinances
pertaining to subject not embraced in this code, shall remain in full force and
effect unless herein repealed expressly or by necessary implications.
§ 10.30 ORDINANCES WHICH AMEND OR SUPPLEMENT CODE.
   (A)   If the legislative body shall desire to amend any existing chapter or
section of this code, the chapter or section shall be specifically repealed and
a new chapter or section, containing the desired amendment, substituted in its
place.
   (B)   Any ordinance which is proposed to add to the existing code a new
chapter or section shall indicate, with reference to the arrangement of this
code, the proper number of the chapter or section. In addition to an indication
thereof as may appear in the text of the proposed ordinance, a caption or title
shall be shown in concise form above the ordinance.
§ 10.31 SECTION HISTORIES; STATUTORY REFERENCES.
   (A)   As histories for the code sections, the specific number and passage
date of the original ordinance, and amending ordinances, if any, are listed
following the code section.
   (B)   (1)   If a statutory cite is included in the history, this indicates
that the text of the section reads substantially the same as the statue.
      (2)   If a statutory cite is set forth as a “statutory reference”
following the text of the sedition, this indicates that the reader should refer
to that statute for further information.
§ 10.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   Any person violating any of the provisions, or failing to comply with
any of the mandatory requirements of any ordinance of the city, is guilty of a
misdemeanor. Except in cases where a different punishment is prescribed by any
ordinance of the city, any person convicted of a misdemeanor under the
ordinances of the city shall be punished by a fine not to exceed $500 or by
imprisonment not to exceed six months, or by both such fine and imprisonment.
   (B)   Each such person is guilty of a separate offense for each and every
day during any portion of which any violation of any provision of the
ordinances of the city is committed, continued or permitted by any such person,
and he or she is punishable accordingly.
(Prior Code, § 1.24.010) (Ord. 307, passed - -1979)

GENERAL PROVISIONS
§ 11.01 CORPORATE SEAL.
   (A)   Design.
      (1)   The corporate seal of the city shall be circular in form with inner
and outer circles of rope design.
      (2)   The outer circle shall be one and seven-eighths inches in diameter
and the inner circle shall be one and three-eighths inches in diameter.
      (3)   It shall bear upon the space between the two circles the words
“City of Malta, Montana” and upon the space within the inner circle the words
“Incorporated 1909” and the word “Seal”.
(Prior Code, § 1.08.010)
   (B)   Adoption. The seal described in division (A) above is adopted as the
corporate seal of the city.
(Prior Code, § 1.08.020)
   (C)   Custodian. The City Clerk shall be the custodian of the corporate seal
and shall affix such to all acts requiring to be so authenticated.
(Prior Code, § 1.08.030)
Statutory reference:
   Authorizing cities to adopt seals, see M.C.A. § 7-1-4124(13)
§ 11.02 OFFICIAL NEWSPAPER.
   The Phillips County News, a newspaper of general circulation, is designated
as the official newspaper of the city.
(Prior Code, § 1.12.010)
§ 11.03 WARDS.
   The wards of the city shall be as designated on the zoning map on file in
the city.
(Prior Code, § 1.20.010) (Ord. 439, passed - -2012)
Statutory reference:
   Wards, see M.C.A. § 7-5-4401(3)
ORDINANCES
§ 11.15 STYLE.
   The style of ordinances shall be as follows:
   (A)   “BE IT ORDAINED by the Council of the City of Malta: ... ” and all
ordinances passed by the Council shall be signed by the Mayor or presiding
officer of the Council and attested to by the City Clerk-Treasurer and the
corporate seal of the city affixed thereto, unless vetoed by the Mayor, as
provided in this subchapter.
   (B)   All ordinances, bylaws and resolutions must be passed by the majority
of the Council, approved by the Mayor or the person acting in his or her stead,
and must be recorded in a book kept by the City Clerk-Treasurer, called “the
ordinance book”, and numbered consecutively in the order they are passed or
codified.
   (C)   No ordinance shall be passed containing more than one subject, which
shall be clearly expressed in its title, except ordinances for the codification
and revision of ordinances.
(Prior Code, § 1.16.011) (Ord. 322, passed - -1980)
§ 11.16 POSTING.
   After an ordinance has been passed by the Council, a copy of said ordinance
shall be posted by the City Clerk in not less than three conspicuous places
within the limits of the city as the Council shall direct and prescribe at the
time of the passage of such ordinance.
(Prior Code, § 1.16.021) (Ord. 322, passed - -1980)
§ 11.17 PASSAGE.
   No ordinance shall be passed, or tax assessed or levied, without the consent
of the majority of the Council at which a quorum is present at the meeting, and
no ordinance shall be passed, except at a regular or adjourned meeting of the
Council unless two-thirds of the whole number of members of the Council vote in
favor thereof and the votes taken thereon in said meeting by yeas and nays
shall be recorded upon the records.
(Prior Code, § 1.16.031) (Ord. 322, passed - -1980)
§ 11.18 PASSAGE OVER VETO.
   In case an ordinance or resolution does not meet the Mayor’s approbation,
the Mayor has power to return the same to the next regular meeting of the
Council with all objections in writing. No ordinance or resolution so vetoed by
the Mayor must go into effect unless the same be afterwards passed by two-
thirds’ vote of the whole number of members of the Council. If the Mayor fails
to return any ordinance or resolution as aforesaid, the same takes effect
without further action.
(Prior Code, § 1.16.041) (Ord. 322, passed - -1980)
§ 11.19 INCORPORATION OF TECHNICAL CODES BY REFERENCE.
   (A)   The Council of the city may adopt Technical Building, Zoning, Health,
Electrical, Fire and Plumbing Codes, in whole or in part by reference.
   (B)   (1)   At least 15 days prior to final action by the Council, a notice
of intent to adopt a technical code, in whole or in part by reference, shall be
published in a newspaper of general circulation in the city.
      (2)   Three copies of the code, or part to be adopted, shall be filed
with the Clerk of the city for inspection by the public.
   (C)   If a technical code, or part of a code, is adopted by reference, a
record in the ordinance book may be made by recording the ordinance without
setting forth the provisions of the code or part of the code adopted.
(Prior Code, § 1.16.051) (Ord. 322, passed - -1980)
§ 11.20 EFFECTIVE DATE.
   No ordinance passed by the Council may become effective until 30 days after
its passage, except:
   (A)   General appropriation ordinances providing for the ordinary and
current expenses of the city; and
   (B)   Emergency measures.
(Prior Code, § 1.16.061) (Ord. 322, passed - -1980)
§ 11.21 DETAILS RELATING TO EMERGENCY MEASURES.
   (A)   In the case of emergency measures, the emergency must be expressed in
the preamble or in the body of the measure, and the measure must receive a two-
thirds vote of all the elected members of the Council.
   (B)   In emergency ordinances, the resolutions shall include only such
measures as are immediately necessary for the preservation of peace, health and
safety, and shall not include:
      (1)   A franchise or license to a corporation or individual;
      (2)   Any provisions for the sale of real estate;
      (3)   Any lease or letting of any property for a period exceeding one
year; or
      (4)   The purchase or sale of real property exceeding $5,000 in value.
(Prior Code, § 1.16.071) (Ord. 322, passed - -1980)
§ 11.22 REPEALED ORDINANCES.
   Whenever any ordinance, or any part of an ordinance, or a resolution is
repealed or modified by a subsequent ordinance or resolution, the ordinance, or
part of an ordinance, or resolution thus repealed or modified, shall continue
in force until the repealing ordinance or the repealing resolution shall go
into effect, or until such time as may be specifically designated in such
repealing ordinances or repealing resolution.
(Prior Code, § 1.16.091) (Ord. 322, passed - -1980)

MAYOR
§ 30.01 DEFINITION.
   The Mayor is the chief executive officer of the city.
(Prior Code, § 2.04.011) (Ord. 321, passed - -1980)
§ 30.02 QUALIFICATIONS.
   The Mayor must be a person:
   (A)   Who is a citizen of the United States;
   (B)   Who is at least 21 years old;
   (C)   Who has been a resident of the state for a period of at least three
years preceding the election to the office of Mayor;
   (D)   Who has been a resident for at least two years preceding the election
to the office of Mayor of the city or an area which has been annexed by the
city;
   (E)   Who is a qualified elector of the city; and
   (F)   The office of Mayor of the city is considered vacant if the individual
elected as Mayor ceases to be a resident of the city.
(Prior Code, § 2.04.021) (Ord. 321, passed - -1980)
§ 30.03 TERM OF OFFICE.
   The Mayor shall hold office for a term of four years and until the
qualification of his or her successor. The term of office of Mayor shall
commence on the date specified by the statutes of the state.
(Prior Code, § 2.04.031) (Ord. 321, passed - -1980)
§ 30.04 DUTIES.
   The Mayor shall devote so much of his or her time to the duties of his or
her office as an efficient and faithful discharge thereof may require.
(Prior Code, § 2.04.041) (Ord. 321, passed - -1980)
§ 30.05 POWERS.
   The Mayor has power to:
   (A)   Nominate and, with the consent of the Council, appoint all non-
elective officers of the city provided for by the City Council, except as
provided by the statutes of the state;
   (B)   Suspend and, with the consent of the City Council, remove any non-
elective officer, stating in the suspension or removal the cause therefor;
   (C)   Supervise the discharge of all official duty by all subordinate
officers;
   (D)   Request that the governor call out the militia to aid the mayor in
suppressing riots or other disorderly conduct, preventing and extinguishing
fires, securing the peace and safety of the city or town or carrying into
effect any law or ordinance (M.C.A. § 7-4-4403);
   (E)   To appoint, with the advice and consent of the City Council:
      (1)   One City Treasurer;
      (2)   One Chief of Police; and
      (3)   Any other officers necessary to carry out the provisions of the
ordinances of the city and the statutes of the state.
   (F)   Cause the ordinances of the city to be executed;
   (G)   Approve all ordinances and resolutions of the City Council adopted by
it;
   (H)   Veto any objectionable part of a resolution or ordinance and approve
the other parts;
   (I)   In case an ordinance or resolution does not meet the Mayor’s
approbation, the Mayor has power to return the same to the next regular meeting
of the City Council with all objections in writing. No ordinance or resolution
so vetoed by the Mayor shall go into effect unless the same be afterwards
passed by two-thirds of the full number of members of the City Council;
   (J)   If the Mayor fails to return any resolution or ordinance as above set
forth, the same takes effect without further action;
   (K)   Communicate to the City Council at the beginning of every session, and
more often if necessary, a statement of the affairs of the city with such
recommendations as the Mayor deems proper;
   (L)   Recommend to the City Council such measures connected with the public
health, cleanliness and ornament of the city, and the improvement of the
government and finances as the Mayor considers expedient;
   (M)   Call special meetings of the City Council. When so called by the
Mayor, the Mayor must state by message the object of the special meeting and
the business of the meeting shall be restricted to the object stated;
   (N)   Cause to be presented, once in three months, a full statement of the
financial condition of the city;
   (O)   Bid for the city on any property sold at a tax or judicial sale
whenever the city is an interested party;
   (P)   Procure and have in his or her custody the seal of the city or town;
   (Q)   Take and administer oaths;
   (R)   Perform such other duties as may be prescribed by law or by resolution
or ordinance of the City Council;
   (S)   The Mayor is the presiding officer of the Council and must sign the
journals thereof and all warrants on the city treasury; and
   (T)   To decide all ties which may result from the vote of the City Council.
The Mayor has no other vote.
(Prior Code, § 2.04.051) (Ord. 321, passed - -1980)
§ 30.06 POWER TO GRANT PARDONS.
   The Mayor has power to grant pardons and remit fines and forfeitures for
offenses against city ordinances when, in the Mayor’s judgment, public justice
would be so served. The Mayor must report all pardons granted, with the reasons
therefor, to the next City Council meeting.
(Prior Code, § 2.04.061) (Ord. 321, passed - -1980)
§ 30.07 CONTRACT SIGNING AUTHORITY.
   The Mayor is authorized and empowered to sign his or her name officially
for, and on behalf of, the city on all contracts, including deeds, bonds,
bills, notes, obligations and other agreements, documents and instruments to
which the city is a party, and to require that the conditions and the said
instruments are faithfully performed, and to borrow money on the credit of the
city when authorized by the City Council.
(Prior Code, § 2.04.071) (Ord. 321, passed - -1980)
§ 30.08 REWARDS; EMPOWERED TO OFFER.
   The Mayor, whenever he or she deems it expedient, is empowered to offer a
reward not exceeding $100 for the arrest and conviction of any person charged
with violating any of the provisions of the municipal code.
(Prior Code, § 2.04.081) (Ord. 321, passed - -1980)
§ 30.09 ACCOUNTS AND REPORTS OF OFFICERS.
   The Mayor shall have the power, when he or she deems it necessary, to
require any officer of the city to exhibit his or her accounts or other papers,
and to make reports to the Council in writing touching upon any subject or
matter pertaining to his or her office.
(Prior Code, § 2.04.091) (Ord. 321, passed - -1980)
§ 30.10 MEETINGS; CALLED TO ORDER; WHEN.
   (A)   The City Council shall hold its open public regular meetings for the
transaction of municipal business on the second and fourth Tuesdays of each
month commencing at a time set by resolution. The Mayor or, in his or her
absence, the President of the City Council shall convene and call the City
Council meeting to order. In the absence of both the Mayor and President of the
City Council, the City Council may appoint one of its number to act in his or
her place. All meetings shall be held in a place provided therefor by City
Council.
   (B)   If a quorum City Council is convened by either the physical presence
of the members or by means of electronic equipment, such as a conference call;
and if the City Council will hear, discuss or act upon a matter over which it
has supervision, control, jurisdiction or advisory power, then the meeting must
be open to the public and the press must be permitted to photograph, televise
or record the proceedings of the meeting, and legally sufficient minutes of the
meeting must be kept and made available for the public.
(Prior Code, § 2.04.093) (Ord. 321, passed - -1980)
§ 30.11 SPECIAL MEETINGS.
   (A)   Special meetings may be called by the Mayor, or at the request of
three members of the Council, at any time by the City Clerk on request, after
giving reasonable notice thereof in writing to all the members of the Council
present in the city.
   (B)   The business of special meetings must be restricted to the object
stated in the notice of the special meeting.
   (C)   All meetings shall be held in a place provided therefor by the City
Council.
(Prior Code, § 2.04.094) (Ord. 321, passed - -1980)
§ 30.12 ORDER OF BUSINESS.
   (A)   At all meetings of the City Council, the order of business to be
followed by the Mayor shall be as follows:
      (1)   Approve minutes of the last regular meeting and minutes of special
or intervening meetings. Minutes will not be read out loud, and corrections
shall be made, if necessary;
      (2)   Approval of the agenda;
      (3)   Review and approve payment of claims/payroll;
      (4)   Reports of standing committees;
      (5)   Reports of special committees;
      (6)   Presentations of petitions and communications;
      (7)   Public comment;
      (8)   Unfinished business;
      (9)   New business; and
      (10)   Other comments.
   (B)   For good cause, the Mayor may, upon motion and majority vote, change
the order of business.
(Prior Code, § 2.04.095) (Ord. 321, passed - -1980)
§ 30.13 ROBERT’S RULES OF ORDER.
   The proceedings of the Council shall, in all cases, be governed by Robert’s
Rules of Order, so far as the same are applicable.
(Prior Code, § 2.04.096) (Ord. 321, passed - -1980)
CITY COUNCIL
§ 30.25 QUALIFICATIONS.
   A Council member must be a person:
   (A)   Who is a citizen of the United States;
   (B)   Who is at least 21 years of age;
   (C)   Who has been a resident of the city for at least two years immediately
preceding his or her election or appointment;
   (D)   Who is a qualified elector of the city; and
   (E)   Who has been a resident for at least 60 days preceding the election to
office of the ward electing him or her, or of an area which has been annexed by
the city and placed in the ward.
(Prior Code, § 2.08.011) (Ord. 320, passed - -1980)
§ 30.26 TERM OF OFFICE.
   (A) Except as provided in division (B) below, a Council member shall hold
office for a term of four years and until the qualification of a successor.
   (B)   (1)   At the first annual election held after the organization of a
city under this title, the electors of the city shall elect two Council members
from each ward, who shall, at the first meeting of the Council, decide by lot
their terms of office, with one from each ward to hold for a term of four years
and one for a term of two years and until the qualification of their
successors.
      (2)   In the succeeding elections, one Council member from each ward must
be elected for a four-year term.
Statutory reference:
   Related provisions, see M.C.A. § 7-4-4402
§ 30.27 GENERAL POWERS.
   The Council has power to make and pass all bylaws, ordinances, orders and
resolutions, not repugnant to the Constitution of the United States or of
Montana, necessary for the government or management of the affairs of the city,
for the execution of powers vested in the city and for carrying into effect the
provisions of the statutes of the state.
(Prior Code, § 2.08.031) (Ord. 320, passed - -1980)
§ 30.28 PRESCRIBING DUTIES OF OFFICERS.
   The Council may prescribe the duties of all city officers and fix their
compensation.
(Prior Code, § 2.08.041) (Ord. 320, passed - -1980)
§ 30.29 PRESCRIBING DUTIES OF OFFICERS NOT OTHERWISE PROVIDED FOR.
   (A)   The City Council has power to prescribe the duties of all officers of
the city, subject to the limitations of the statutes of the state.
   (B)   The duties of the Street Commissioner, Chief of the Fire Department
and other city officers not prescribed by the statutes of the state may be
prescribed by ordinance.
(Prior Code, § 2.08.051) (Ord. 320, passed - -1980)
§ 30.30 DETERMINATION OF VACANCY IN MUNICIPAL OFFICE.
   If any officer moves from the city, or any Council member from his or her
ward, such office must be declared vacant by the Council.
(Prior Code, § 2.08.061) (Ord. 320, passed - -1980)
§ 30.31 FILLING OF VACANCY.
   When any vacancy occurs in any elective office, the Council, by a majority
vote of the members, may fill the same for the unexpired term and until the
qualification of the successor. The vacancy in the office of Council member
must be filled from the ward in which the vacancy exists; but, if the Council
shall fail to fill such vacancy before the time for the next election, the
qualified electors of such city or ward may nominate and elect a successor to
such office.
(Prior Code, § 2.08.071) (Ord. 320, passed - -1980)
§ 30.32 REMOVAL OF APPOINTED OFFICER.
   The Council, on written charges to be entered upon its journal after notice
to the party, and after trial by Council, may remove any non-elected officer by
vote of two-thirds of the members elect.
(Prior Code, § 2.08.081) (Ord. 320, passed - -1980)
§ 30.33 SALARY OF OFFICERS.
   The Council shall determine, by resolution, the salaries and compensation of
elected and appointed city officers.
(Prior Code, § 2.08.091) (Ord. 320, passed - -1980)
§ 30.34 OFFICERS OF COUNCIL.
   (A)   At the first regular meeting of the New Year, the Council shall elect
a President who, in the absence of the Mayor, is the presiding officer of the
Council and may perform the duties of Mayor.
   (B)   In the absence of the President, the Council may appoint one of its
number to act in his or her place.
(Prior Code, § 2.08.092) (Ord. 320, passed - -1980)
§ 30.35 MEETINGS.
   (A)   (1)   The Council shall hold its open public regular meetings for the
transaction of municipal business on the second and fourth Tuesdays of each
month commencing at a time by resolution. The Mayor or, in his or her absence,
the President of the Council shall convene and call the Council meeting to
order.
      (2)   In the absence of both the Mayor and President of the Council, the
Council may appoint one of its members to act in his or her place. All meetings
shall be held in a place provided therefor by the Council.
   (B)   If a quorum Council is convened by either the physical presence of the
members or by means of electronic equipment, such as a conference call, and if
the Council will hear, discuss or act upon a matter over which it has
supervision, control, jurisdiction or advisory power, then the meeting must be
open to the public and the press must be permitted to photograph, televise or
record the proceedings of the meeting, and legally sufficient minutes of the
meeting must be kept and made available for the public.
(Prior Code, § 2.08.093) (Ord. 320, passed - -1980)
§ 30.36 SPECIAL MEETINGS.
   Special meetings open to the public may be called by the Mayor, or at the
request of three members of the Council, at any time by the City Clerk on
request, after giving reasonable notice thereof in writing to all members of
the Council present in the city. The business of special meetings must be
restricted to the object stated in the notice of special meeting.
(Prior Code, § 2.08.094) (Ord. 320, passed - -1980)
§ 30.37 POWER TO MAKE AND EXECUTE CONTRACTS.
   The Council has power to make any and all contracts necessary to carry into
effect the powers granted to it by the state and to provide for the matter of
executing the same.
(Prior Code, § 2.08.095) (Ord. 320, passed - -1980)
§ 30.38 COMPENSATION AND DUTIES OF CITY EMPLOYEES.
   The Council shall fix the compensation and prescribe the duties of all
employees of the city subject to limitations of the statutes of the state.
(Prior Code, § 2.08.096) (Ord. 320, passed - -1980)
§ 30.39 REPORTS FROM MUNICIPAL OFFICERS.
   The Council has power to require from an officer at any time a report in
detail of the transactions in his or her office or any matter connected
therewith.
(Prior Code, § 2.08.097) (Ord. 320, passed - -1980)
§ 30.40 CONDUCT OF COUNCIL BUSINESS.
   (A)   A majority of the members of the Council constitute a quorum for the
transaction of business, but a less number may meet and adjourn at a time
stated, and may compel the presence of absent members under such rules and
penalties as the council may prescribe.
   (B)   The ayes and nays must be called and recorded on the final passage of
any ordinance by law or resolution or the making of any contract. The voting on
the election or appointment of any officer must be viva voce. A majority of the
whole number of members elected is requisite to appoint or elect an officer,
and such vote must be recorded.
(Prior Code, § 2.08.098) (Ord. 320, passed - -1980)
§ 30.41 MINUTES OF MEETINGS; PUBLIC INSPECTION.
   (A)   (1)   Appropriate minutes of all meetings required by M.C.A. § 2-3-203
to be open must be kept and must be available for inspection by the public.
      (2)   If an audio recording of a meeting is made and designated as
official, the recording constitutes the official record of the meeting. If an
official recording is made, a written record of the meeting must also be made
and must include the information specified in division (B) below.
   (B)   Minutes must include without limitation:
      (1)   The date, time and place of the meeting;
      (2)   A list of the individual members of the public body, agency or
organization who were in attendance;
      (3)   The substance of all matters proposed, discussed or decided; and
      (4)   At the request of any member, a record of votes by individual
members for any votes taken.
   (C)   If the minutes are recorded and designated as the official record, a
log or time stamp for each main agenda item is required for the purpose of
providing assistance to the public in accessing that portion of the meeting.
   (D)   Any time a presiding officer closes a public meeting pursuant to
M.C.A. § 2-3-203, the presiding officer shall ensure that minutes taken in
compliance with division (B) above are kept of the closed portion of the
meeting. The minutes from the closed portion of the meeting may not be made
available for inspection except pursuant to a court order.
Statutory reference:
   Related provisions, see M.C.A. § 2-3-203
§ 30.42 COUNCIL RULES AND DISCIPLINE.
   The Council may determine the rules of its proceedings, punish its members
for improper conduct and expel any member for the same by a two-thirds’ vote of
the members elected.
(Prior Code, § 2.08.100) (Ord. 320, passed - -1980)
§ 30.43 CONTROL OF NUISANCES.
   The Council shall define and abate nuisances and impose fines upon persons
guilty of creating, continuing or suffering a nuisance to exist upon the
premises which they occupy or control.
(Prior Code, § 2.08.101) (Ord. 320, passed - -1980)
§ 30.44 CITY JUDGE.
   The Council may, by ordinance, determine whether the office of City Judge
shall be filled by appointment by the said City Council or by election.
(Prior Code, § 2.08.102) (Ord. 320, passed - -1980)
CHAPTER 31: OFFICERS AND EMPLOYEES
Section
General Provisions
   
31.01   Officers’ bonds

GENERAL PROVISIONS
§ 31.01 OFFICERS’ BONDS.
   (A)   Required. All elected or appointed city officers and employees shall
be bonded in such sums as provided in this section.
(Prior Code, § 2.48.010)
   (B)   State supervision. The amount for which a city officer or employee or
group of officers or employees shall be bonded is subject to the supervision of
the Department of Administration of the state. If the Department of
Administration determines that the amount of the bond is inadequate, it may
require the City Council to purchase an adequate bond.
(Prior Code, § 2.48.020)
   (C)   Form.
      (1)   The condition of such surety bond must be that the principal shall
well, truly and faithfully perform all official duties required of him or her
by law and also such additional duties as may be imposed on him or her by any
law of the state or city subsequently enacted and that he or she will account
for and pay over and deliver to the person or officer entitled to receive the
same all moneys or other property that may come into his or her hands as such
officer.
      (2)   The principal and sureties on the official bond are also in all
cases liable for the neglect, default or misconduct in office of any deputy,
clerk or employee appointed or employed by such principal.
      (3)   The form of the surety bond for city officers and employees must be
approved by the City Attorney and filed and recorded in the office of the City
Clerk.
(Prior Code, § 2.48.030)
   (D)   Insurer selection.
      (1)   The City Council shall purchase a blanket surety bond covering city
officers and employees.
      (2)   The City Council shall actively solicit offers on a competitive
basis from available, qualified insurance or surety companies before purchasing
the bond.
      (3)   Such blanket surety bond purchased by the City Council shall be
executed by responsible insurance or surety companies authorized and admitted
to execute surety bonds in the state.
(Prior Code, § 2.48.040)
   (E)   Premium payment. The premiums for such blanket surety bond shall be a
proper charge against the budget of the city’s General Fund.
(Prior Code, § 2.48.050)
   (F)   Coverage. The bond herein mentioned shall be a blanket bond and shall
cover all officers and employees of the city or any group or combination of
officers and employees.
(Prior Code, § 2.48.060)
   (G)   Amount.
      (1)   The City Treasurer shall be bonded in the sum of $20,000.
      (2)   All other officers and employees shall be bonded in the sum of
$5,000.
(Prior Code, § 2.48.070)
(Ord. 333, passed - -1982; Ord. 377, passed - -1990)
§ 31.02 SALARIES.
   Salaries for officials and employees shall be as set by City Council from
time to time.
(Prior Code, § 2.64.010)
SPECIFIC OFFICES
§ 31.15 CITY ATTORNEY.
   (A)   Appointment. The Mayor, subject to the consent and approval of the
Council, shall appoint a City Attorney who shall hold office for the duration
of his or her appointment or until his or her successor is appointed and
qualified.
(Prior Code, § 2.12.010)
   (B)   Qualification; term of office.
      (1)   The City Attorney to be appointed shall be a person who has been
licensed to practice as an attorney in the state.
      (2)   He or she shall hold his or her office until suspended or removed
as provided by this section.
(Prior Code, § 2.12.020)
   (C)   Duty.
      (1)   It shall be the duty of the City Attorney to attend before the City
Court and other courts of the city and the District Court, and prosecute on
behalf of the city, and he or she shall generally do and perform such other
acts as pertain to the office of the Council. He or she shall, when required,
draw for the use of the Council contracts and ordinances for the government of
the city and, when required, give to the Mayor or Council written opinions on
questions pertaining to the duties and the rights, liabilities and powers of
the city.
      (2)   Nothing herein shall be taken or construed as preventing the
Council from employing other and additional counsel in special cases and
providing for the payment of such services. The City Attorney may be suspended
or removed from office by the Council for the neglect, violation or disregard
of the duties required by this section or the ordinances of the city.
(Prior Code, § 2.12.030)
Statutory reference:
   City attorneys, see M.C.A. §§ 7-4-4601 et seq.
§ 31.16 CLERK-TREASURER.
   (A)   Consolidation of offices.
      (1)   The office of City Clerk and the office of City Treasurer shall be
consolidated into one office to be known as the city’s “Clerk-Treasurer
Office”.
      (2)   The Mayor, with the advice and consent of the Council, shall
appoint an official to bear the title of City Clerk-Treasurer who shall be the
head of the office of City Clerk-Treasurer.
      (3)   The office of City Treasurer is abolished.
      (4)   The office of City Clerk is abolished.
(Prior Code, § 2.18.010)
   (B)   Reference to office. Whenever in the municipal code of the city, or in
any ordinance or resolution of the city, the terms “City Treasurer” or “City
Clerk” (or “Treasurer” or “Clerk”, where such terms clearly refer to the City
Treasurer or the City Clerk) shall appear, such term shall be deemed to refer
to and shall be replaced by the term “City Clerk-Treasurer”.
(Prior Code, § 2.18.020)
(Ord. 342, passed - -1984; Ord. 368, passed - -1988)
§ 31.17 DUTIES OF CITY CLERK-TREASURER RELATED TO ADMINISTRATION.
   (A)   Attend all meetings of the Council and record and sign the proceeding
thereof and all ordinances, bylaws, resolutions and contracts passed, adopted
or entered into;
   (B)   Enter in a book all ordinances, resolutions and bylaws passed and
adopted by Council;
   (C)   Countersign and cause to be published or posted, as provided by law,
all ordinances, bylaws or resolutions passed and adopted by the Council;
   (D)   Sign, number and keep a record of all licenses, commissions or permits
granted or authorized by the Council;
   (E)   Take and administer oaths, but must not charge or receive any fees
therefor; and
   (F)   Perform such other and further duties as the Council may prescribe.
Statutory reference:
   Related provisions, see M.C.A. § 7-4-4501
§ 31.18 DUTIES OF CITY CLERK-TREASURER RELATED TO CITY RECORDS AND PAPERS.
   The City Clerk-Treasurer shall:
   (A)   File and keep all records, books, papers or property belonging to the
city and deliver the documents or property to the Clerk-Treasurer’s successor
when qualified;
   (B)   Make and certify copies of all records, books, and papers in the
Clerk-Treasurer’s possession on the payment of fees that are allowed county
clerks, which must be paid into the city treasury; and
   (C)   Make and keep a complete index of the journal, ordinance book, finance
book and all other books and papers on file in the clerk’s office.
Statutory reference:
   Related provisions, see M.C.A. § 7-4-4502
§ 31.19 CITY ORDINANCE BOOK.
   The book required by M.C.A. § 7-4-4501(b) is called “The Ordinance Book”.
Statutory reference:
    Related provisions, see M.C.A. § 7-4-4503

§ 33.01 ESTABLISHMENT.
   The Justice Court of the county is hereby designated to act as the City
Court in all matters and cases arising under and out of violations of state law
and any and all ordinances of the city.
(Prior Code, § 2.56.010) (Ord. 369, passed - -1989)
§ 33.02 FUNDING.
   The Mayor and the Clerk-Treasurer are hereby authorized to provide for the
city’s share of the funding for such court by entering into an agreement with
the county for proportionate sharing of the costs of salaries, training and
office expenses between the city and the county, as nearly as is reasonably
practicable.
(Prior Code, § 2.56.020) (Ord. 369, passed - -1989)
§ 33.03 ANNUAL REVIEW.
   Such interlocal agreement between the city and county shall be reviewed
annually and shall be subject to approval by resolution of the City Council and
the County Commissioners.
(Prior Code, § 2.56.030) (Ord. 369, passed - -1989)
CHAPTER 34: CIVIL DEFENSE
Section
   
34.01   Plan approved; purpose
   
34.02   Mayor and Board of County Commissioners; duties
   
34.03   Director’s duties
§ 34.01 PLAN APPROVED; PURPOSE.
   The county and city civil defense plan is approved. This plan provides for
an integrated city-county organization for civil defense and for operations
during periods of emergency and thereby constitutes the most effective and
efficient means of meeting the civil defense needs of the city and its citizens
by making maximum use of the existing agencies and capabilities of local
government within the county, supported by volunteers and non-governmental
personnel and resources, to prevent or minimize loss of life and property that
could be caused by enemy attack or other catastrophe or disaster affecting the
city. The Mayor is authorized to approve such revisions of the civil defense
plan as may be made from time to time if he or she deems the revisions to be
reasonably necessary to meet the civil defense needs of the city and its
citizens.
(Prior Code, § 2.60.010)
§ 34.02 MAYOR AND BOARD OF COUNTY COMMISSIONERS; DUTIES.
   The Mayor and the Board of County Commissioners shall, during periods of
emergency caused by enemy attack or other catastrophe or disaster affecting the
city, jointly direct and control the operations of the city-county organization
for civil defense established in the civil defense plan. The Mayor is
authorized and directed to take, during such periods of emergency, such actions
as are reasonably necessary to prevent or minimize loss of life and property in
cooperation with the Board of County Commissioners and the Civil Defense
Director of the county.
(Prior Code, § 2.60.020)
§ 34.03 DIRECTOR’S DUTIES.
   (A)   The County Civil Defense Director, under policy guidance of the Board
of County Commissioners in coordination with the Mayor, is responsible to
conduct the following day to day activities:
      (1)   Recommending actions, preparing budget requests, training,
assignment of personnel;
      (2)   Licensing, marking and stocking of public shelters;
      (3)   Preparation of program paper, administration of civil defense
program;
      (4)   Coordination of the program with all departments, development of
civil defense plan and supporting documents for approval by the Mayor and
Commissioners of the county.
   (B)   The Civil Defense Director will act as chief of staff to the
executives of the county and city.
(Prior Code, § 2.60.030)

Section

GENERAL PROVISIONS
§ 35.01 DEPOSITORIES.
   The First State Bank of Malta, Montana, and the Bank of Malta, Montana, are
each designated as an official depository for municipal funds of the city.
(Prior Code, § 3.04.010) (Ord. 291, passed - -1972)
FUNDS
§ 35.15 SPECIAL SIDEWALK, CURB AND GUTTER FUND.
   (A)   Created. The City Council hereby creates the “Malta Special Sidewalk,
Curb and Gutter Fund”, for the purpose of providing means for the construction
of sidewalks, curbs and gutters, or any combination thereof, which may
hereafter be constructed by order of the City Council under the provisions of
§§
152.015 through
152.021 of this code of ordinances.
(Prior Code, § 3.12.010)
   (B)   Form. An application shall be submitted to Council by an owner(s) of
real property located within the city limits. The application must be include a
contractor’s invoice stating the cost of the repair/construction of the
sidewalk, curbs or gutters requested by the applicant. The city will issue
checks from the city’s Sidewalk, Curbs or Gutter Fund to pay the contractor for
his or her services. The loans shall bear interest at the rate of 7% per annum,
levying an annual assessment and tax against each lot or parcel of land upon
which sidewalks, curbs of gutters have been constructed pursuant to the
application. The principal and interest on the loan are paid in seven annual
equal instalments.
(Prior Code, § 3.12.020)
   (C)   Levy of assessment and tax.
      (A)   The City Council shall, annually, and before the first Monday in
September of each year, pass and adopt a resolution levying an assessment and
tax against each lot or parcel of land in front of which sidewalks, curbs and
gutters, or any combination thereof, have been constructed under orders of the
City Council, pursuant to §§
152.015 through
152.021 of this code of ordinances.
      (B)   Said resolution levying such assessments shall be in every manner
prepared and certified the same as resolutions levying assessments for the
making of improvements in special improvement districts.
(Prior Code, § 3.12.040)
   (D)   Delinquent taxes. No checks shall be drawn from said fund for
construction of sidewalk, curb and gutters on any lot, parcel or property for
which there are owed to the city or any political subdivision of the state any
delinquent taxes or assessments.
(Ord. 386, passed - -1992)
§ 35.16 CAPITAL IMPROVEMENT PROGRAM FUND.
   (A)   Fund created. The City Council does hereby create the “Malta Capital
Improvement Program Fund” for the purpose of replacement and acquisition of
property, plant or equipment costing in excess of $5,000, with a life
expectancy of five years or more, as authorized by M.C.A. § 7-6-616.
(Prior Code, § 3.16.010)
   (B)   Allocation. The City Council, by resolution, determines the purpose of
capital improvement program funds and will, by resolution, determine the amount
of funds to be allocated to the Capital Improvement Program Fund.
(Prior Code, § 3.16.020)
   (C)   Warrants. Warrants drawn against the city’s Capital Improvement
Program Fund will be made in the excess of $5,000 for the replacement of
property, plant or equipment with a life expectancy of five years or more.
(Prior Code, § 3.16.030)
(Ord. 374, passed - -1989)
§ 35.17 UNDERGROUND AUTOMATIC LAWN SPRINKLER FUND.
   (A)   Created. The City Council hereby creates the “Malta Underground
Automatic Lawn Sprinkler Fund”, for the purpose of conserving water by the
construction of underground automatic lawn sprinklers, which may hereafter be
constructed by order of the City Council under the provisions of §§
52.40 through
52.41 of this code of ordinances.
(Prior Code, § 3.18.010)
   (B)   Form. An application shall be submitted to Council by an owner(s) of
real property located within the city limits. The application must be include a
contractor’s invoice stating the cost of the underground automatic lawn
sprinklers. The city will issue checks from the Underground Automatic Sprinkler
Fund to pay the contractor for his or her services. The loans shall bear
interest at the rate of 7% per annum, levying an annual assessment and tax
against each lot or parcel of land upon which underground automatic sprinkler
have been constructed pursuant to the application. The principal and interest
on the loan are paid in seven annual equal instalments.
(Prior Code, § 3.18.020)
   (C)   Levy of assessment and tax. The City Council shall, annually, and
before the first Monday in September of each year, pass and adopt a resolution
levying an assessment and tax against each lot or parcel of land upon which
underground automatic lawn sprinklers have been constructed under orders of the
City Council pursuant to §§
52.40 through
52.41 of this code of ordinances. Said resolution levying such assessments
shall be in every manner prepared and certified the same as resolutions levying
assessments for the making of improvements in special improvement districts.
(Prior Code, § 3.18.040)
   (D)   Delinquent taxes. No warrants shall be drawn from said fund for
construction of an underground automatic lawn sprinkler on any lot, parcel or
property for which there are owed to the city or any political subdivision of
the state any delinquent taxes or assessments.
(Prior Code, § 3.18.050)
(Ord. 398, passed - -2001)

§ 50.01 OFFICER IN CHARGE; APPOINTMENT; ENFORCEMENT DUTY; POWER TO ARREST; TO

   (A)   The Public Works Director (PWD) of the city is oversees the city
landfill and shall enforce the provisions of this chapter.
(Prior Code, § 8.20.010)
   (C)   No person shall convey any ashes, manure, garbage, junk or refuse
matter to and upon the city dump ground unless he or she deposits or
distributes the same at such dump ground in such manner and at such point
thereon and during such hours of the day as may be directed by Public Works

(Prior Code, § 8.20.030)

CHAPTER 51: GARBAGE
Section
   
51.01   Definition
   
51.02   Contract, equipment purchase and hiring authority

§ 51.01 DEFINITION.
   The word GARBAGE, as used in this chapter, is intended to mean solid waste
as defined by M.C.A. § 75-10-103(7): “‘Solid waste’ means all putrescible and
non-putrescible wastes, including, but not limited to, garbage, rubbish,
refuse, ashes, sludge from sewage treatment plants, water supply treatment
plants, or air pollution control facilities; construction and demolition
wastes; dead animals, including offal; discarded home and industrial
appliances; and wood products or wood byproducts and inert materials. ‘Solid
waste’ does not mean municipal sewage, industrial wastewater effluents, mining
wastes regulated under the mining and reclamation laws administered by the
department of state lands, slash and forest debris regulated under laws
administered by the Department of Natural Resources and Conservation, or
marketable byproducts.”
(Prior Code, § 8.16.010) (Ord. 388, passed - -1993)
§ 51.02 CONTRACT, EQUIPMENT PURCHASE AND HIRING AUTHORITY.
   The city shall provide for the disposal of all garbage within the city and,
to that end, shall have the power to contract with some responsible person,
firm, corporation or other business organization and/or the City Council is
hereby authorized and empowered to purchase equipment and hire personnel for
the removal of the garbage and other refuse accumulated within the city.
(Prior Code, § 8.16.020) (Ord. 388, passed - -1993)
§ 51.03 CONTRACT; PRELIMINARY PROCEDURE; BOND.
   Before the letting of any contract for the collection and removal of garbage
and other refuse within the city limits, the city council shall advertise for
bids pursuant to state law and amendments thereto. Upon the letting of such a
contract, the person, firm, corporation or other business organization
receiving the same shall give a bond to the city in such sum as shall be
designated by the City Council, which bond shall provide for the faithful
performance of such contract.
(Prior Code, § 8.16.030) (Ord. 388, passed - -1993)
§ 51.04 COST TO BE ASSESSED AGAINST REAL ESTATE.
   The cost of collection of garbage from streets, alleys, business
establishments and private premises in the city shall in all cases be assessed
or charged against the real estate from which said garbage is generated and
removed.
(Prior Code, § 8.16.040) (Ord. 388, passed - -1993)
§ 51.05 MONTHLY INSTALLMENTS.
   (A)   The property owner’s choice to have the yearly garbage fees and
assessments divided into 12 installments and paid monthly as of December 21,
2001, shall apply to all subsequent years.
   (B)   It is the owners of property receiving garbage collection services
from the city shall be solely
responsible for the payment of all charges for garbage collection services.
(Prior Code, § 8.16.045) (Ord. 408, passed - -2001)
§ 51.06 OWNER TO PROVIDE CONTAINERS, CONTAINER RACKS.
   The city shall provide garbage containers; 300-gallon garbage cans will be
placed in the alleys to be used by those living in the area and 90-gallon
garbage cans will be provided to residents that do not have an alley behind
their residents.
§ 51.07 PREPARATION OF GARBAGE AND OTHER REFUSE.
   Trimmings resulting from trimming or removing trees, or hedges or shrubs
shall be hauled to the city landfill; no landfill fees will be charged.
§ 51.08 BURNING PROHIBITED.
   (A)   The burning of garbage, as defined herein, within the corporate limits
of the city, in or out of incinerators, is hereby prohibited and any such
burning shall be deemed a violation of this chapter.
   (B)   Any owner, occupant, tenant, lessee or other person having control of
any land within the city limits of the city who deposits or permits to be
deposited any burning garbage or material of any kind, nature or substance, or
any ashes, coals, cinders or other residue of burning garbage or materials in
any garbage container or who deposits or who permits to be deposited any such
material at the landfill of the city, shall be guilty of a misdemeanor and,
upon conviction thereof, shall be punished as hereinafter provided. Such
burning materials or residue thereof shall be disposed of only in such manner
as shall be directed by the city’s Health Officer.
(Prior Code, § 8.16.170) (Ord. 388, passed - -1993) Penalty, see §
51.99
§ 51.09 NON-GARBAGE WASTE.
   Building rubbish resulting from new construction or extensive alterations to
buildings or yards or from the removal of large trees, and any trade wastes,
chemicals, compounds or other contaminants are not garbage under this chapter
and must be otherwise disposed of at the expense of the person responsible for
its production.
(Prior Code, § 8.16.180) (Ord. 388, passed - -1993) Penalty, see §
51.99
§ 51.10 HAZARDOUS ACCUMULATION OF WASTE MATTER.
   (A)   (1)   The city’s Public Works Director supervises garbage collection
or any of their authorized representatives may order the owner, occupant,
tenant, lessee or agent of the owner of any premises upon which there is an
accumulation of any rubbish, ashes, garbage or other waste matter to remove the
same within a reasonable time if such accumulation is:
         (a)   Offensive to sight;
         (b)   In a condition which fosters the propagation of rats or vermin
or flies or other insects; or
         (c)   Otherwise unsanitary, prejudicial or in any manner hazardous to
the public health.
      (2)   Such order shall be made in writing and delivered, whenever
feasible, personally to the owner, occupant, tenant, lessee or agent of the
owner or, where such personal delivery is not feasible, posted conspicuously at
the premises. Such order shall specify a reasonable period within which
compliance shall be had.
   (B)   For purposes of ascertaining violations of this section and
investigating complaints made hereunder, whenever reasonable cause for
investigation appears, the right of entry onto any premises at a reasonable
time to conduct a reasonable inspection or investigation is hereby granted to
the city’s Health Officer, the agency in charge of garbage collection or any of
their authorized representatives.
   (C)   In the event that any order lawfully issued in pursuance of division
(A) above is not complied with in such reasonable time as is specified, the
particular instance of improper accumulation or storage of rubbish, ashes or
garbage is hereby declared to be a nuisance and may be summarily abated, at the
expense of the violator, by the city’s Health Officer, the agency in charge of
garbage collection or any of their authorized representatives.
   (D)   It shall be unlawful to hinder, prevent or refuse to permit any lawful
inspection or investigation authorized in pursuance of division (B) above.
   (E)   Concrete, fence posts, tires, large pieces of lumber, large tree limbs
or large containers of used cooking oil shall not be placed in the city garbage
cans. The above items are to be hauled to the city landfill.
(Prior Code, § 8.16.190) (Ord. 388, passed - -1993) Penalty, see §
51.99
§ 51.11 MONTHLY AND YEARLY GARBAGE RATES
   Garbage charges be set by resolution.
§ 51.12 RATE TABLE.
   The rate table for units of charges by type of user will be set by
resolution.
§ 51.99 PENALTY.
   Any person, firm or corporation, who either directly or indirectly, or by
his, her or its servant, agent or employee, shall violate any of the provisions
of this chapter shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor and, upon conviction,
shall be punished by a fine of not more than $250 or by imprisonment in the
jail for not more than 12-1/2 days or by both such fine and imprisonment. Each
day of continuing violation of this chapter shall be deemed a separate offense
for purposes of the penalties prescribed by this section.
(Prior Code, § 8.16.200) (Ord. 388, passed - -1993)

GENERAL PROVISIONS
§ 52.01 PUBLIC WORKS DIRECTOR; APPOINTMENT.
   (A)   Generally. The Public Works Director shall be the general executive
officer of the waterworks and shall have charge of employees and all property
pertaining to the waterworks system.
      (1)   He or she shall give written orders for all supplies and materials
and preserve a copy of such orders in his or her office and shall have charge
of all contracts, and shall see that they are faithfully performed.
      (2)   He or she shall have charge of the alteration, erection or repair
of all buildings, engines, pumps, fixtures, wells, reservoirs and grounds. He
or she shall determine the location and size of all water mains, service
connections, valves, hydrants and specials.
   (B)   Records. He or she shall keep a correct record of all mains, hydrants,
valves and specials. He or she shall submit all bills, payrolls and accounts to
the Council for its approval.
   (C)   Books and papers. He or she shall have the care and safekeeping of all
books and papers belonging to the Water Department and shall deliver same to
his or her successor in office.
   (D)   Valves and hydrants. He or she shall see that the valves and hydrants
are restored to their proper positions after they have been used by the Fire
Department, and shall see that all breaks or defects are promptly repaired.
   (E)   Inspection. Whenever, in the judgment of the Superintendent, he or she
deems it necessary, he or she may cause an inspection of the premises of any
consumer for the purpose of examining into the condition of all pipes, meters
and water fixtures.
   (F)   Meters. He or she shall also keep a true record of all meters in use
and examine them when necessary and shall test any meters he or she suspects of
inaccurate measurement and remedy the cause.
(Prior Code, § 13.04.020)
(Ord. 394, passed - -1995)
§ 52.02 WATER CLERK; DUTIES.
   The job description and duties of the Water Clerk shall be set by
resolution.
(Prior Code, § 13.04.030)
§ 52.03 RULES AND REGULATIONS PART OF CONTRACT.
   The rules and regulations in this chapter are established for the
management, control and protection of the city waterworks. These rules shall be
considered a part of the contract with every person who takes water supplied by
the city from the city waterworks, and every person taking water shall be
considered as having expressed consent to be bound thereby.
(Prior Code, § 13.04.040) (Ord. 394, passed - -1995)
§ 52.04 APPLICATION; CONTENTS; CONTRACT REQUIREMENTS.
   (A)   Application for use of water must be made at the City Clerk’s office
on printed forms furnished for that purpose. The application must be made by
the agent or owner of the property to be benefitted, describing the lot, block
and street where water is desired, and shall state fully all the purposes for
which the water may be required, and shall sign a contract therefor. No taps
will be made to the mains until the applicant for whom such connections are to
be made has signed the contract mentioned in this section and a plumber’s
permit has been issued authorizing a plumber to lay such pipes and connections
as will conform to the application. Additionally, the applicant will pay the
city a hookup fee of $500 when hooking up structures to the main or installing
new curb stops.
   (B)   A fee will not be charged to owners of empty lots who are connecting
to an existing curb stop to install a water hydrant on their empty lots to be
used for lawn watering. If, later, the landowner builds on the property $500
shall be paid and the existing pit meter will be removed and a meter will be
installed in the new structure.
(Prior Code, § 13.04.050) (Ord. 450, passed - -2017)
§ 52.05 CORPORATION STOP AND SADDLE FURNISHED.
   The city shall furnish the corporation stop and saddle; all other materials
shall be furnished by the applicant.
(Prior Code, § 13.04.060) (Ord. 394, passed - -1995)
§ 52.06 WATER SHUT OFF REQUESTS.
   (A)   Should it be desired to discontinue the use of water, a written notice
(work order) thereof must be filed in the City Clerk’s office, and all charges,
current and in arrears, paid. Water rates will continue to be charged even
though the water is shut off.
   (B)   The Public Works Director shall turn off the water to such premises
without charge. The owner or his or her agent may have service restored to the
premises whether or not physical shut off was possible by written notice to the
office of the City Clerk and payment of $15.
(Prior Code, § 13.04.070) (Ord. 394, passed - -1995; Ord. 397A, passed - -1996)
§ 52.07 RATES PAID MONTHLY; DELINQUENCIES.
   (A)   Water charges must be paid monthly at the City Clerk’s office by 3:00
pm on the twentieth day of the month. If the twentieth of the month falls on a
Friday, Saturday or Sunday the payment will be due by 8:00 am on the Monday
after the twentieth. If payment is not paid by the due date and time, a 10%
penalty fee will be added to all past due charges.
   (B)   When the customer’s account is owing three months, the city will send
the water account’s property owner a water termination notice by certified mail
at least ten days before the proposed water shut off date.
      (1)   The notice shall state the amount due that must be paid in full by
8:00 am on the twentieth of the month or payment arrangements made with the
City Clerk-Treasurer.
      (2)   If the amount owed is not paid in full or payment arrangements made
with the City Clerk by 8:00 am on the date of water service termination, an
additional $75 penalty fee will be assessed. The total amount owed and the
additional $75 fee must be paid in full before water service is restored. If
the twentieth of the month falls on a Friday, Saturday and Sunday, the payment
will be due by 8:00 am on the Monday after the twentieth of the month. In no
case will the city terminate water service on a Friday, Saturday or Sunday.
§ 52.08 SEPARATE CONNECTIONS REQUIRED.
   Two or more premises, whether owned by the same owner or by separate owners,
cannot be supplied from one and the same connection.
(Prior Code, § 13.04.090) (Ord. 394, passed - -1995)
§ 52.09 STOP AND WASTE COCK REQUIRED.
   Every service pipe must be furnished with a stop and waste cock placed
within one foot after the pipe enters the building. This stop must have a
handle or wrench attached to turn same and be in working order so that water
can be readily shut off and drained from pipes, and so that the premises can be
protected in case of leaks.
(Prior Code, § 13.04.100) (Ord. 394, passed - -1995)
§ 52.10 LOCATION OF STOP BOXES AND CUTOFFS.
   All stop boxes and cutoffs for controlling the supply of water to consumers
shall be placed within the street line in the location designated by the Public
Works Director. The top of all stop boxes shall conform to the surface of the
sidewalk or contour of the ground.
(Prior Code, § 13.04.110) (Ord. 394, passed - -1995)
§ 52.11 COPPER OR PVC WITH LOCATOR LINE ATTACHED.
   Consumers will be required to use, in making connections with the city water
mains within the street lines, copper pipe or PVC pipe with locator line
attached.
(Prior Code, § 13.04.120) (Ord. 394, passed - -1995)
§ 52.12 PRIVATE HYDRANT REQUIREMENTS.
   No private hydrant shall be located on the sidewalk or any place of easy
access to the public unless metered, and then only by special permit.
(Prior Code, § 13.04.130) (Ord. 394, passed - -1995)
§ 52.13 CITY NOT RESPONSIBLE FOR PIPES OR FIXTURES.
   The city shall not be responsible for pipes and fixtures. All owners, at
their expense, must keep service pipes from city mains and all their apparatus
in good working order and properly protected from frost and other dangers. No
claim shall be made against the city on the account of the breaking of any
service pipe or apparatus or for accidental failure in supply of water. No
reduction from the regular rates will be made for any time that service pipes
or fixtures may be frozen. Owners abandoning any service line will be required
to turn off the supply at the corporation stop and shall be responsible for all
expenses for the abandonment.
(Prior Code, § 13.04.140) (Ord. 394, passed - -1995)
§ 52.14 RESTRICTIONS DURING FIRE ALARMS.
   During all fire alarms, the use of hoses, yard fountains, hydraulic motors,
elevators and all outlets where a constant flow of water is maintained, is
positively forbidden.
(Prior Code, § 13.04.150) (Ord. 394, passed - -1995) Penalty, see §
52.99
§ 52.15 CERTAIN ACCIDENTS NOT CITY’S RESPONSIBILITY.
   The city will not be held responsible for accidents resulting from insecure
boilers or from variations in water pressure or the ram of the water from the
mains or collapse from any cause whatsoever.
(Prior Code, § 13.04.160) (Ord. 394, passed - -1995)
§ 52.16 CITY’S RIGHT TO MAKE REPAIRS.
   (A)   The city reserves the right at any time to shut off its mains for the
purpose of making repairs or extensions or any other purpose and no claim shall
be made against the city by reason of the breaking of any service pipe or
service cock or from any other damage that may result from shutting off water
for repairing, laying or relaying mains, hydrants or other connections.
Expenses for repairs to service lines or curb cocks shall be the owner’s
responsibility.
   (B)   (1)   The city shall have the right to require the owner to repair any
broken, damaged or leaking service pipe, service line or service cock, at the
owner’s expense. The failure of an owner to make the repairs requested by the
city may result in the termination of water service. The city shall provide
written notice of the need for repairs to the owner. The owner shall have 48
hours to have a licensed plumber on the site to begin the repairs.
      (2)   The repairs shall be completed within a reasonable amount of time.
The city may grant an extension of time if a licensed plumber, hired by the
owner, requests an extension of time because the plumber would not be able to
start the repairs within the 48-hour time limit.
   (C)   If the owner fails to make the repairs within the time allowed by the
city, then the city may proceed to make the repairs and bill the costs of those
repairs to the owner. City employees are authorized to do the repair work. The
cost of the repairs shall be added to the owner’s other water charges and may
be collected as allowed by ordinance for water charges, or as otherwise allowed
by law. If the owner fails to pay the costs of the repairs within 30 days, the
city may terminate water service to the owner’s property until such time as the
cost of repairs, penalty and interest are paid in full.
(Prior Code, § 13.04.170) (Ord. 394, passed - -1995; Ord. 424, passed - -2006)
§ 52.17 CONTRACTORS OR BUILDERS DESIRING WATER.
   Contractors, builders or others desiring water for building purposes must
make application to the Public Works Director, who will issue a permit
therefor. The amount to be paid shall be based upon the rates fixed therefor.
(Prior Code, § 13.04.180) (Ord. 394, passed - -1995)
§ 52.18 UNLAWFUL ACTS.
   It is unlawful for any person to use or take water from any part of the
waterworks of the city without a license or a permit, or who shall, without
authority from the Water Department, open or hitch to, dig out, curb over or
remove any fireplug or hydrant, stopcock, valve, valve box or any other fixture
appertaining to the waterworks, or shall turn on or shut off water into or from
any water pipe wherever situated.
(Prior Code, § 13.04.200) (Ord. 394, passed - -1995) Penalty, see §
52.99
§ 52.19 WATER RATES CHARGED TO OWNER.
   The water rates as set forth in §
52.25 of this chapter shall be charged to the owner of the premises to which
the water is furnished. If, from any cause whatsoever, any sums owing for water
furnished to the premises shall become delinquent, the Public Works Director
shall shut off the water to such premises and in no case shall the water
service to such premises be restored until the delinquencies and all other
charges have been paid in full. Change of ownership or change in tenants
occupying the premises in question shall not affect the application of this
section.
(Prior Code, § 13.04.210) (Ord. 394, passed - -1995)
§ 52.20 OWNER RESPONSIBLE.
   (A)   It is declared and enacted by the City Council that owners of property
receiving water services from the city shall be solely responsible for the
payment of all charges for water services and any other fees and expenses for
receiving water services.
   (B)   Failure of the owner of property receiving water services to pay water
charges, fees and expenses for water services shall be grounds for the Public
Works Director to turn off the water services to such property as provided in §
52.20 of this chapter and shall also be subject to such other penalties
provided in this chapter.
(Prior Code, § 13.04.211) (Ord. 394, passed - -1995)
§ 52.21 TAPS PROHIBITED.
   No person but an authorized employee of the Waterworks Department or a
licensed plumber under the supervision of the Public Works Director and/or his
or her designee shall make any tap or connection with any main or distributing
pipe of the waterworks system.
(Prior Code, § 13.04.220) (Ord. 394, passed - -1995) Penalty, see §
52.99
§ 52.22 INSPECTION AND ENTRANCE AUTHORIZED.
   The Public Works Director of the city waterworks or other officer or
employee of the city shall be permitted at all times to enter the premises or
buildings of consumers to examine the water pipes and fixtures, and the manner
in which the water is used. Installation, maintenance and removal of water
meters shall be included as a permitted entrance to the consumer’s premises or
buildings. If a consumer refuses to grant access to his or her premises or
buildings for the purposes set forth herein, water to such premises and
buildings shall be shut off. To have water service restored, the consumer or
owner must first allow access, pay all charges, current and arrears and the
turn-on fee of $75.
(Prior Code, § 13.04.230) (Ord. 394, passed - -1995; Ord. 428, passed - -2007)
§ 52.23 LICENSED PLUMBERS ONLY.
   No person, except a regularly licensed plumber under the supervision of the
Public Works Director and/or his or her designee, will be permitted to do any
work on any pipes or connections made with the mains or water supply of the
city waterworks. Any plumbers failing to perform their work according to the
established rules and regulations therefor or executing it unskillfully or to
the detriment of the city waterworks may be prohibited from making connections
with the city mains.
(Prior Code, § 13.04.240) (Ord. 394, passed - -1995) Penalty, see §
52.99
§ 52.24 MONTHLY WATER RATES.
   Water charges for water furnished by the municipal water system of the city
will be set by resolution.
(Prior Code, § 13.04.250) (Ord. 394, passed - -1995)

   The rate table for units of charges by type of user will be set by
resolution.
(Prior Code, § 13.04.260) (Ord. 394, passed - -1995)
§ 52.26 STREET OPENING FEE.
   (A)   It is declared and enacted by the City Council that the owners of
property receiving water services from the city shall be solely responsible for
the payment of a street opening fee whenever a property owner or water user
excavates or opens any city street or public right-of-way for the purposes of
servicing or making repairs to the owner’s pipes, fixtures and/or property. The
street opening fee shall be established by resolution of the City Council.
   (B)   Failure of the owner of the property receiving water services to pay
the street opening fee shall be grounds for the Public Works Director to turn
off the water services of such property as provided in §
52.21 of this chapter and shall also be subject to such other penalties as
provided in this chapter.
(Prior Code, § 13.04.270) (Ord. 403, passed - -2001)
§ 52.27 CONSENT TO ANNEXATION AS A REQUIREMENT FOR RECEIVING SERVICES.
   (A)   Any person, firm or corporation receiving or applying to receive water
or sewer services outside the incorporated city limits shall be required to
consent to the annexation of the tract of property served by the city water
and/or sewer as a condition of receiving such services. This consent shall be
written in such form so that it may be recorded and be a binding covenant that
runs with the land.
   (B)   The city shall not be obligated to annex the property even if a
consent is signed and services are provided. Failure to execute a consent shall
be grounds for the termination of services to the tract of property.
(Prior Code, § 13.04.280) (Ord. 402, passed - -2001)
§ 52.28 FURNISHING WATER SERVICES TO PERSONS LOCATED OUTSIDE THE CITY LIMITS.
   (A)   It is declared and enacted by the City Council that the city may
furnish water services to any person, factory or industry located outside the
corporate limits of the city at reasonable rates filed by the city and
approved, when otherwise required by statute, by the Public Service Commission.
   (B)   Collections for furnishing water services shall be in the same manner
as collections are made with the corporate limits.
(Prior Code, § 13.04.290) (Ord. 400, passed - -2001)

   (A)   When sprinkling, watering or irrigating with water from the municipal
water system, care must be exercised to prevent the waste of water.
   (B)   It is unlawful to cause water to overflow from a garden, lawn or
boulevard, or to use excessive amounts of water, or to waste water in any other
manner.

§ 52.41 UNDERGROUND AUTOMATIC LAWN SPRINKLERS.
   (A)   Requirements. The City Council is hereby authorized to create and
amend requirements and specifications for the construction of underground
automatic lawn sprinklers in conjunction with the city’s special Underground
Automatic Lawn Sprinkler Fund by passage of a resolution of the City Council.
   (B)   “Underground automatic lawn sprinklers” defined. An UNDERGROUND
AUTOMATIC LAWN SPRINKLER is defined as any system of pipes and fittings placed
underground and designed and constructed in accordance with the requirements
and specifications set by resolution of the City Council, with the purpose to
sprinkle or irrigate a lawn, garden, trees or boulevard.
   (C)   No liability. The city shall not be liable for any loss arising out of
the construction or use of any underground automatic lawn sprinkler to the
owner or any third party and any liability shall be the sole responsibility of
the owner of the real property or other person who designed, constructed or
maintained the underground automatic lawn sprinkler.

   (A)   Any person violating any provision of this chapter for which no
specific penalty is prescribed shall be subject to §
10.99 of this code of ordinances.
   (B)   (1)   Section
52.15 of this chapter will be strictly enforced and, if violated, will subject
the offender, on conviction, to a fine of not less than $50.
(Prior Code, § 13.04.150)
      (2)   Any person violating §
52.19 of this chapter shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor and, upon
conviction thereof, shall be fined not less than $500 or imprisoned in the
county jail for not more than six months, or by both such fine and
imprisonment.
(Prior Code, § 13.04.200)
   (C)   If any person performs any act declared unlawful by §§
52.40 through
52.41 of this chapter, the Public Works Director is authorized and empowered to
turn off the water supply to the property being watered or irrigated
unlawfully. In order to restore the water supply to such property, a $25 fee
must be paid by the owner, tenant, manager or occupant of the property to the
City Clerk. Upon payment of the fee, the City Clerk will notify the Public
Works Director of such payment who then will restore the water supply to the
property.
