GENERAL PROVISIONS
§ 150.001 HOUSE NUMBERING.
   (A)   Method. In order to establish a uniform system of numbering houses
within the city, all houses fronting on streets and avenues within the city
shall be numbered in conformity with the following provisions.
      (1)   Even numbers shall be on north and west sides of streets and
avenues of the city, and odd numbers shall be on the south and east sides of
the same.
      (2)   Numbering shall commence at the east side of the city and increase
running west 100 numbers to the block, on all streets within the city; and upon
all avenues shall commence on Front Street and increase running south 100
numbers to the block. Numbering upon the properties lying upon the north side
of the Great Northern right-of-way shall be as set forth in the plat on file
with the City Clerk.
      (3)   As to all locations within the city, a plat has been prepared
following the rules as set forth above in this section, which plat is on file
with the City Clerk and in which plat each portion and parcel of land within
the city has been appropriately numbered, and the numbers so designated upon
said plat are adopted as the official numbering for all property within the
city.
(Prior Code, § 12.20.010)
   (B)   Designation by City Clerk. The City Clerk shall designate the number
of all houses in conformity with the plat as provided for in division (A) above
and shall furnish the owner of each house now or, hereafter built with its
proper number as soon as completed. When any house is not correctly numbered,
or not numbered at all, the City Clerk shall give such house its proper number
and require the same to be placed upon such house in a conspicuous place next
to the street or avenue, as the case may be, at the expense of the owner,
including the cost of furnishing the number.
(Prior Code, § 12.20.020)
(Ord. 194, passed - -1964)
Statutory reference:
   Authorizing cities to number houses, see M.C.A. § 7-15-4101
§ 150.002 FIRE LIMITS.
   Beginning with the intersection of the centerline of the main tract of the
Great Northern Railway Company in the city and the centerline produced of South
First Avenue West in the city, then with said South First Avenue West southerly
to its intersection with the centerline of the alley of Block 5 of Trafton’s
first addition to the city; thence easterly along the centerline of said alley
to the west line of Lot 11 produced in said Block 5; thence southerly along the
west line of said Lot 11 to the centerline of South Third Street East; thence
easterly along the centerline of South Third Street East to its intersection
with the centerline of South First Avenue East; thence northerly along the
centerline of South First Avenue East to its intersection with the centerline
of South Second Street East; thence easterly along the centerline of South
Second Street East to its intersection with the centerline of South Second
Avenue East; thence northerly along the Great Northern Railway Company; thence
westerly along the centerline of the main track of the Great Northern Railway
Company to the point of beginning, shall constitute and be known as the fire
limits of the city.
(Prior Code, § 15.32.010) (Ord. 185, passed - -1942; Ord. 243, passed - -1949;
Ord. 259, passed - -1956)
§ 150.003 PETROLEUM STORAGE TANKS.
   (A)   Permit application; notification of property owners. When any person,
persons, firm or corporation is desirous of constructing, altering,
maintaining, repairing or moving any petroleum products storage tanks in the
city limits of the city, he, she or they shall make application to the City
Clerk for a permit for that purpose, and the provisions of Ord. 1861 shall be
followed with regard to the receipt of said application and its submission to
the Council; except that, the City Clerk, in giving notice to all property
owners of the application, shall notify by mail all of such property owners
within a radius of 300 feet of the proposed location.
(Prior Code, § 15.44.010)
   (B)   Permit required. It is unlawful hereafter for any person or persons,
firm or corporation to erect, place or locate, or cause to be erected, placed
or located, any petroleum products storage tanks above or below the ground in
the city without first having obtained a permit from the City Council therefor.
(Prior Code, § 15.44.020)
   (C)   Permit; city’s right to deny issue; location restriction.
      (1)   A permit shall not issue as a matter of right; for the welfare of
its inhabitants and the protection from fire, and in the exercise of its police
powers, the city, in its discretion, may issue or refuse to issue a permit to
any person, persons, firm or corporation for the erection of additional
petroleum products storage tanks within the limits of the city, unless the same
are placed upon the right-of-way of the Great Northern Railroad Company.
      (2)   It is the policy of the city not to increase the number of
petroleum products storage tanks now existing indiscriminately about the city,
and to confine them so far as possible to the same general locality, this being
along the Great Northern Railroad right-of-way through the city.
(Prior Code, § 15.44.030)
(Ord. 233, passed - -1946)
CODES ADOPTED
§ 150.015 BUILDING CODE.
   (A)   Municipal Building Code adopted.
      (1)   (a)   The state’s Building Code, including all model technical
codes, appendices, amendments and modifications adopted by the state’s
Department of Labor and Industry (or its successor), Building Codes Bureau,
applicable to local government jurisdictions, as set out in the administrative
rules of the state and as amended from time to time by the Building Codes
Bureau, shall be adopted by reference by an administrative order of the Mayor,
as authorized by M.C.A. § 50-60-301(1)(b), as the Municipal Building Code of
the city.
         (b)   For those jurisdictions certified to enforce the Building Code,
the following codes and rules must be adopted:
            1.   International Building Code, 2012 edition, as amended by
A.R.M. § 24.301.146;
            2.   International Energy Conservation Code, 2003 edition, as
provided by A.R.M. § 24.301.161;
            3.   International Existing Building Code, 2006 edition, as
provided by A.R.M. § 24.301.171; and
            4.   International Residential Code, 2012 edition, as provided by
A.R.M. § 24.301.154.
      (2)   The application of the Municipal Building Code is limited to
residential buildings containing less than five dwelling units or their
attached-to structures, any farm or ranch building, and any private garage or
private storage structure used only for the owner’s own use located within the
city limits, as provided by M.C.A. § 50-6-102(1)(a). The Building Codes Bureau
shall have Building Code jurisdiction over all other buildings and structures
as well as Electrical, Plumbing and Mechanical Code jurisdiction over all
buildings.
      (3)   The Municipal Building Code shall regulate the erection,
construction, enlargement, alteration, repair, moving, removal, demolition,
conversion, occupancy, equipment, use, height, area and maintenance of those
buildings and/or structures within the city which are subject to the Municipal
Building Code, and shall provide for the issuance of permits and collection of
fees and penalties.
      (4)   Within 30 days after notice by the Building Codes Bureau of any
amendments to the state’s Building Code which apply to local government
jurisdictions, an administrative order adopting such amendments shall be
prepared and signed by the Mayor. The administrative order is effective 30 days
after it is signed.
(Prior Code, § 15.04.010)
   (B)   Copies on file. One copy of the Municipal Building Code shall be on
file in the office of the City Clerk.
(Prior Code, § 15.04.020)
   (C)   Application; jurisdictional area. This section and the code herein
adopted by reference shall be applicable to all buildings situated within the
corporate limits of the city.
(Prior Code, § 15.04.030)
(Ord. 359, passed - -1987; Ord. 410, passed - -2002; Ord. 418, passed - -2004;
Ord. 420, passed - -2004; Ord. 426, passed - -2007; Ord. 427, passed - -2007;
Ord. 443, passed - -2015)
§ 150.016 ENERGY CONSERVATION CODE.
   The City Council adopts the International Energy Conservation Code, 2003
edition, as provided by A.R.M. § 24.301.161, a copy of which is on file in the
office of the City Clerk.
(Prior Code, § 15.16.010) (Ord. 420, passed - -2004; Ord. 427, passed - -2007)
BUILDING CODE ENFORCEMENT
§ 150.030 PURPOSE.
   In order to enable the adoption and enforcement of certain building codes
and procedures, the city council adopts this chapter which shall govern the
application of and procedure under the current editions of certain building
codes, which have been or may hereafter be adopted by the city, including, but
not limited to, the following:
   (A)   International Building Code, 2006 edition, as amended by A.R.M. §
24.301.146, upon adoption and as amended by the Department of Labor and
Industry, Building Codes Bureau;
   (B)   International Residential Code, 2006 edition, as provided by A.R.M. §
24.301.154, and applicable amendments thereto, upon adoption and as amended by
the Department of Labor and Industry, Building Codes Bureau;
   (C)   International Energy Conservation Code, 2003 edition, as provided by
A.R.M. § 24.301.161, upon adoption and as amended by the Department of Labor
and Industry, Building Codes Bureau;
   (D)   International Existing Building Code, 2006 edition; and
   (E)   Part II, uniform federal accessibility standards, upon adoption and as
amended by the Department of Labor and Industry, Building Codes Bureau.
(Prior Code, § 15.64.010) (Ord. 363, passed - -1987; Ord. 410, passed - -2002;
Ord. 418, passed - -2004; Ord. 420, passed - -2004; Ord. 426, passed - -2007;
Ord. 427, passed - -2007)
§ 150.031 APPLICATION AND JURISDICTION.
   The provisions of this subchapter shall apply to all buildings situated
within the corporate limits of the city.
(Prior Code, § 15.64.020) (Ord. 363, passed - -1987)
§ 150.032 PERMITS REQUIRED; APPLICATION; REVIEW; EXPIRATION.
   (A)   No building or structure shall be erected, moved, added to or
structurally altered without a building permit issued by the Building Official.
The Building Official shall be responsible for plan review coordination and for
the issuance of building permits.
   (B)   Upon application by any person for a building permit, the Building
Official shall review plans submitted in connection with the application for
compliance with all Building Codes adopted and in force in the city. In
addition, the Building Official shall submit such plans to any other affected
city department for review and approval by that department, before issuance of
a building permit.
   (C)   The Building Official shall complete the building plan review and
shall either issue or deny the issuance of a building permit within 30 days of
submittal by the applicant.
   (D)   The Building Official may, in proper cases, request the aid of the
Department of Labor and Industry, Building Codes Bureau, other state agencies
or professional consultants to aid in coordination of plan review. If the
assistance of such agencies or consultants is sought by the Building Official,
then plan review and issuance or non-issuance of a building permit shall be
completed within 40 days of submittal by the applicant.
   (E)   All applications for building permits shall be made on such forms as
may be provided by the Building Official and shall contain such information as
may be required to ensure compliance with all Building Codes. At the minimum,
such information shall include, but shall not be limited to, the following:
      (1)   A scale drawing showing the dimensions of the lot or parcel;
      (2)   The location of existing and proposed structures on such lot or
parcel;
      (3)   The legal description of the lot or parcel;
      (4)   The proposed use of the land, building or other structures situated
thereon; and
      (5)   Name of property owner.
   (F)   Building permits issued hereunder shall expire 180 days from the date
of issuance, unless construction pursuant to the building permit has commenced.
Once commenced, if construction thereafter is suspended or abandoned for more
than 180 days, the building permit shall expire. Upon expiration of a building
permit, a new building permit must be sought and issued pursuant to the
procedures set forth in this section.
(Prior Code, § 15.64.030) (Ord. 363, passed - -1987; Ord. 418, passed - -2004;
Ord. 426, passed - -2007)
§ 150.033 INSPECTIONS.
   (A)   Inspections shall be conducted by the Building Official. The Building
Official shall review all plans and applications for building permits for
compliance with this chapter both before and during construction. If, during
the course of an inspection, the Building Official finds that an application
for a building permit, or the construction work, does not comply with this
subchapter, he or she shall so inform the applicant or owner of such non-
compliance and shall order any further construction or work to be stopped until
such time as the plans or the construction work, or both, conform to the
requirements of this subchapter.
   (B)   Where other departments or agencies require inspections, the Building
Official shall ensure that such inspections are conducted in a timely fashion
so as not to cause undue delay in construction.
   (C)   All inspections and issuance of certificates of occupancy shall be
conducted in accordance with the current edition of the Building Code, as the
same now exists or may hereafter be amended.
(Prior Code, § 15.64.040) (Ord. 363, passed - -1987; Ord. 426, passed - -2007)
§ 150.034 STAFF; QUALIFICATIONS AND DUTIES.
   The Building Official shall be the Building Inspector. The Building Official
shall be a person with at least three years of experience in the building
construction trade and shall have all of those powers and duties set forth in
the current edition of the Building Code, as now existing or as may hereafter
be amended and, to the extent possible, those powers and duties set forth in
M.C.A. Title 50, Chapter 60, as now existing or as may hereafter be amended.
(Prior Code, § 15.64.050) (Ord. 363, passed - -1987; Ord. 418, passed - -2004)
§ 150.035 FACTORY-BUILT BUILDINGS.
   (A)   Factory-built buildings which are approved by the Department of Labor
and Industry, Building Codes Bureau, shall be subject to inspection and fees
under this subchapter only for purposes of compliance with zoning, utility
connection and foundation requirements.
   (B)   Applications to the Building Official for erection of and utility
connections for factory-built buildings shall be in accordance with the
provisions of this chapter; provided, however, that, fees for building permits
for and inspections of factory-built buildings shall be one-half of such fees
for other buildings subject to this subchapter.
(Prior Code, § 15.64.060) (Ord. 363, passed - -1987; Ord. 418, passed - -2004)
§ 150.036 PERMIT AND INSPECTION FEES.
   Building permit and inspection fees shall be charged and collected in
accordance with International Building Code § 108. All fees charged hereunder
shall be collected by the city’s Clerk-Treasurer.
(Prior Code, § 15.64.070) (Ord. 363, passed - -1987; Ord. 418, passed - -2004)
§ 150.037 BOARD OF APPEALS.
   (A)   In order to determine the suitability of alternative materials and
methods of construction, and to provide for reasonable interpretations of the
provisions of this subchapter and any Building Codes adopted by and effective
in the city, there is created a Board of Appeals consisting of five members who
shall be qualified by experience and training to pass upon matters pertaining
to building construction and who are not employees of the city.
   (B)   The Building Official shall be an ex officio member of and shall act
as Secretary to the Board of Appeals.
   (C)   The Board of Appeals shall be appointed by the Mayor of the city,
subject to the approval of the City Council, and the Board of Appeals shall
hold office at the pleasure of the Mayor.
   (D)   The Board of Appeals shall adopt rules of procedure for conducting its
business and shall render all decisions and findings in writing to the
appellant with a duplicate copy to the Building Official.
(Prior Code, § 15.64.080) (Ord. 363, passed - -1987; Ord. 426, passed - -2007)
BUILDING SETBACKS
§ 150.050 SETBACK FROM CURB REQUIRED.
   Any person, firm, corporation or other entity desiring to build, or erect,
construct or place any building or structure on any lot or parcel of ground in
the city, except in the business or commercial areas of the city, must build,
erect, construct or place such building or structure so that no part or portion
of such building or structure shall be closer than 30 feet to the curb or
curbline of such lot or parcel of ground.
(Prior Code, § 15.48.010) (Ord. 328, passed - -1982)
§ 150.051 ESTABLISHMENT OF CURBLINE.
   In the event there is no established curb, the City Engineer shall establish
a curbline and the same shall be used for the location of any building or
structure on any lot or parcel of ground next to such curbline established by
the City Engineer, except in business or commercial areas of the city.
(Prior Code, § 15.48.020) (Ord. 328, passed - -1982)
§ 150.052 SETBACK ON CORNER LOTS.
   On corner lots or parcels of ground located in the city, no part or portion
of a building or structure shall be closer than 30 feet to a curb or curbline
established by the City Engineer, except in business or commercial areas of the
city.
(Prior Code, § 15.48.030) (Ord. 328, passed - -1982)
§ 150.053 SETBACK FROM SIDE OR REAR LOT LINE.
   Buildings or structures built, erected, constructed or placed on lots or
parcels of ground located within the residential area of the city must have a
minimum distance of three feet between the furthest projecting part of the
building or structure and the property line on the side or rear of the lot or
parcel of ground on which such building or structure shall be built, erected,
constructed or placed.
(Prior Code, § 15.48.040) (Ord. 328, passed - -1982)
§ 150.054 VARIANCE.
   Any variances or exceptions to the provisions of this subchapter must be
approved by the Building Official and the City Council.
(Prior Code, § 15.48.050) (Ord. 328, passed - -1982)
§ 150.055 BUSINESS OR COMMERCIAL AREAS.
   In business or commercial areas in the city, any buildings or structures to
be built, erected, constructed or placed on lots or parcels of ground in such
business or commercial area may be closer to the curb or curbline if approved
by the Building Official and the City Council.
(Prior Code, § 15.48.060) (Ord. 328, passed - -1982)
§ 150.056 PLANS REQUIRED.
   All applications for building permits submitted to the City Clerk for
approval by the City Council must indicate the location of such building or
structure on the lot or parcel of ground on which it is to be built, erected,
constructed or placed. The City Council shall reject any application for a
building permit not showing the location of such building or structure in
relation to its distance from the curb or curbline.
(Prior Code, § 15.48.070) (Ord. 328, passed - -1982)
§ 150.057 APPLICATION FOR BUILDING PERMIT.
   All applications for building permits must be submitted to the City Clerk at
least five days before the Council meeting at which the application for permit
is to be reviewed by the City Council. Applications shall be upon standard
forms available from the City Clerk. Upon receipt of an application for a
building permit, the City Clerk shall notify, in writing, each owner or
occupant of property within 150 feet of the lot or parcel of ground on which
the building or structure is to be built, erected, constructed or placed,
informing such owner or occupant when the application for building permit will
be considered by the City Council and informing such owner or occupant that a
protest against the granting of the building permit for such building or
structure may be made, either orally at the stated meeting or in writing to the
City Clerk. The notice to be given by the City Clerk to owners and occupants of
property within 150 feet of the lot or parcel of ground on which the building
or structure is to be built, erected, constructed or placed shall briefly
describe the proposed building or structure and its location upon the lot or
parcel of ground where it is to be built, erected, constructed or placed.
(Prior Code, § 15.48.080) (Ord. 328, passed - -1982)
ACCESSIBILITY STANDARDS
§ 150.070 UNIFORM FEDERAL ACCESSIBILITY STANDARDS ADOPTED.
   The City Council adopts and incorporates herein by this reference that
certain building code known as the Uniform Federal Accessibility Standards,
part II, and all amendments, additions and modifications made thereto (herein
collectively called the “Code”), being particularly the current edition of the
code upon adoption by and as amended from time to time by the Building Code
Bureau of the Department of Commerce (or its successor) of the state.
(Prior Code, § 15.56.010) (Ord. 360, passed - -1987)
§ 150.071 COPIES ON FILE.
   Copies of the current edition of the Code, as adopted and amended, shall be
filed with the Clerk-Treasurer of the city for inspection by the public.
(Prior Code, § 15.56.020) (Ord. 360, passed - -1987)
§ 150.072 APPLICATION; JURISDICTIONAL AREA.
   This subchapter and the Code herein adopted by reference shall be applicable
to all federal and federally-financed buildings and facilities situated within
the corporate limits of the city.
(Prior Code, § 15.56.030) (Ord. 360, passed - -1987)
§ 150.999 PENALTY.
   (A)   Any person violating any provision of this chapter for which no
specific penalty is prescribed shall be subject to §
10.99 of this code of ordinances.
   (B)   In case any owner, occupant or agent, after having been requested by
the City Clerk to do so, as provided in §
150.001 of this chapter, neglects or refuses for ten days to number a house as
required by §
150.001 of this chapter, or to number or attempt to number such house otherwise
than in conformity with §
150.001 of this chapter, and the requirements, of the City Clerk, such person
shall, upon conviction thereof, be fined not less than $1, nor more than $25,
and, when such fine is paid, the City Clerk shall cause such house to be
correctly numbered at the expense of the city.
(Prior Code, § 12.20.030)
   (C)   Any person violating any provision of §
150.003 of this chapter shall be guilty of a misdemeanor and, upon conviction
thereof, shall be fined in a sum not exceeding $100.
(Prior Code, § 15.44.040)
   (D)   Any person, firm, partnership, corporation or any other entity, as
owner, lessee, sublessee or occupant, violating any of the provisions of §
150.015 of this chapter shall be guilty of a misdemeanor and each such person
or entity shall be deemed guilty of a separate offense for each and every day
or portion thereof during which any violation of any provision of §
150.015 of this chapter is committed, continued or permitted. Upon conviction
of any such violation, such person or entity shall be punished by fine of not
more than $300 or by imprisonment in jail for not more than 90 days, or by both
such fine and imprisonment. Each day of continuing violation of §
150.015 of this chapter shall be deemed a separate offense for the purposes of
the penalties prescribed by this division (D).
(Prior Code, § 15.04.040)
   (E)   (1)   It is unlawful for any person, firm, partnership, corporation or
any other entity, to erect, construct, enlarge, alter, repair, move, improve,
remove, convert or demolish, equip, use, occupy or maintain any building or
structure in the city, or cause or permit the same to be done, contrary to or
in violation of any of the provisions of §§
150.030 through
150.037 of this chapter.
      (2)   Any person, firm, partnership, corporation or other entity
violating any of the provisions of §§
150.030 through
150.037 of this chapter shall be guilty of a misdemeanor, and each such person
or entity shall be guilty of a separate offense for each and every day, or
portion thereof, during which any violation of any of the provisions of §§
150.030 through
150.037 of this chapter is committed, continued or permitted and, upon
conviction of any such violation, such person or entity shall be punished by a
fine of not more than $300 or by imprisonment for not more than 90 days, or by
both such fine and imprisonment.
(Prior Code, § 15.64.090)
   (F)   (1)   Any person, firm, partnership, corporation or any other entity,
as owner, lessee, sublessee or occupant, violating any of the provisions of §§
150.070 through
150.072 of this chapter shall be guilty of a misdemeanor and each such person
or entity shall be deemed guilty of a separate offense for each and every day
or portion thereof during which any violation of any provision of §§
150.070 through
150.072 of this chapter is committed, continued or permitted. Upon conviction
of any such violation, such person or entity shall be punished by fine of not
more than $300 or by imprisonment in jail for not more than 90 days, or by both
such fine and imprisonment. Each day of continuing violation of §§
150.070 through
150.072 of this chapter shall be deemed a separate offense for the purposes of
the penalties prescribed by this division (F)(1).
(Prior Code, § 15.56.040)
      (2)   It is declared that any violation of §§
150.070 through
150.072 of this chapter shall constitute a public nuisance and, in addition to
any other remedies available to the city, the city may bring a civil action to
enjoin the violation of any provisions of §§
150.070 through
150.072 of this chapter.
(Prior Code, § 15.56.050)
(Ord. 194, passed - -1942; Ord. 233, passed - -1946; Ord. 359, passed - -1987;
Ord. 360, passed - -1987; Ord. 363, passed - -1987)
CHAPTER 151: TRAILER COACHES AND PARKS
Section
   
151.01   Definitions
   
151.02   License application; approval
   
151.03   License fees
   
151.04   License revocation or reissuance
   
151.05   License posting required
   
151.06   License transferability
   
151.07   Register of occupants; information required; availability to officials
   
151.08   Parking on dwelling premises
   
151.09   Domestic animals or pets restricted
 
   
151.99   Penalty
§ 151.01 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this chapter, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   MAINTAIN or OPERATE. Applies to a period in excess of two weeks.
   TRAILER COACH. Any vehicle used or so constructed as to permit its being
used as a conveyance upon the public streets or highways and duly licensable as
such and shall include self-propelled and non- self-propelled vehicles so
designated, constructed, reconstructed or added to by means of an enclosed
addition or room is such a manner as will permit the occupancy thereof as a
dwelling or sleeping place for one or more persons and having no foundation
other than wheels, jacks or skirtings when located in a duly licensed trailer
coach park; provided that, such parking sites are equipped with adequate safety
and sanitary facilities as herein described and such other rules and
regulations as are necessary to the health of the residents of trailer coach
parks and immediate adjacent communities.
   TRAILER COACH PARK. Any plot of ground upon and which is prepared for
occupancy by more than one trailer coach, to be occupied for dwelling purposes
and located regardless of whether or not a charge is made for such
accommodations.
   TRAILER COACH SPACE. A plot of ground within a trailer coach park.
(Prior Code, § 5.44.010)
§ 151.02 LICENSE APPLICATION; APPROVAL.
   (A)   Applications for a license shall be filed with and issued by the City
Council through the office of the City Clerk. Applications shall be in writing
signed by the applicant and shall contain the following:
      (1)   The name and address of the applicant;
      (2)   The location and legal description of the trailer coach or trailer
park;
      (3)   Such further information as may be requested by the City Council to
enable it to determine if the proposed location will comply with legal
requirements, including a sketch or plot designating numbered trailer spaces;
and
      (4)   No change or alteration in the plot plan shall be made without
first making a written application for such change or alteration to the City
Council and receiving a written permit therefrom.
   (B)   The City Council shall investigate the location and if it is found to
be in compliance with all provisions of this chapter and all other applicable
chapters or statutes, the application may be approved.
(Prior Code, § 5.44.020)
§ 151.03 LICENSE FEES.
   (A)   Any person who maintains or operates a trailer coach or trailer coach
park must first obtain a license from the City Clerk, which license must be
approved by the City Council and which will be effective for the balance of the
calendar year.
   (B)   The annual fees for such licenses shall be as follows:
      (1)   Trailer coach: $3; and
      (2)   Trailer coach park: $25.
(Prior Code, § 5.44.030)
§ 151.04 LICENSE REVOCATION OR REISSUANCE.
   The City Council may revoke any permit to maintain a trailer coach or
license to maintain and operate a trailer coach park when the person covered
has been found guilty of violating any provisions of this chapter. After such
revocation, a permit or license may be reissued if the circumstance leading to
the revocation has been remedied and the trailer coach or trailer coach park is
maintained and operated in full compliance with this chapter or any other
section of this code pertaining thereto.
(Prior Code, § 5.44.040)
§ 151.05 LICENSE POSTING REQUIRED.
   The permit certificate shall be conspicuously posted on the individual
trailer coach not located within a trailer coach park or in the office of or on
the premises of the trailer coach park at all times.
(Prior Code, § 5.44.050)
§ 151.06 LICENSE TRANSFERABILITY.
   All licenses issued under this chapter shall be personal to the licensee and
be non-transferable without the written consent of the City Council first being
obtained.
(Prior Code, § 5.44.060)
§ 151.07 REGISTER OF OCCUPANTS; INFORMATION REQUIRED; AVAILABILITY TO
OFFICIALS.
   (A)   It shall be the duty of the licensee to keep a register containing a
record of all trailer coach owners that are occupants located within the park.
   (B)   The register shall contain the following information:
      (1)   Name and address of each occupant in each trailer coach;
      (2)   Make, model and year of all automobiles and trailer coaches;
      (3)   License number and owner of each trailer coach and automobile by
which it is towed;
      (4)   The state issuing such license; and
      (5)   The date of arrival and departure of each trailer coach and the
number or other identification of the space or spaces occupied.
   (C)   The park shall keep the register available for inspection at all times
by law enforcement officers, public health officials and other officials whose
duties necessitate acquisition of the information contained in the register.
The register records shall not be destroyed until after a period of three years
following the date of registration.
(Prior Code, § 5.44.070) Penalty, see §
151.99
§ 151.08 PARKING ON DWELLING PREMISES.
   Not more than one trailer coach, motor home or camper may be parked, used
and occupied on the premises of any dwelling; provided, the occupants of the
trailer coach have free access to and the unlimited use of the sanitary
facilities of the dwelling on said premises. A trailer coach, motor home or
camper may be parked, used and occupied within city limits for no more than two
weeks in a single year.
(Prior Code, § 5.44.080) (Ord. 444, passed - -2016) Penalty, see §
151.99
§ 151.09 DOMESTIC ANIMALS OR PETS RESTRICTED.
   No domestic animals or house pets shall be allowed to run at large or commit
any nuisances within the limits of a trailer coach park.
(Prior Code, § 5.44.090) Penalty, see §
151.99
§ 151.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   Any person violating any provision of this chapter for which no
specific penalty is prescribed shall be subject to §
10.99 of this code of ordinances.
   (B)   A violation of §
151.08 of this chapter is a misdemeanor punishable by a fine of not more than
$500, imprisonment in the county jail for not more than six months, or both.
Each day is a separate offense. The city may remove the offending trailer
coach, motor home or camper at the owner’s expense. The city may also enforce §
151.08 of this chapter by seeking injunctive relief in the District Court.
(Prior Code, § 5.44.080) (Ord. 444, passed - -2016)

GENERAL PROVISIONS
§ 152.001 STREET GRADES ESTABLISHED BY AUTHORITY OF CITY COUNCIL; REQUIRED.
   (A)   The grades of all streets, avenues and alleys within the city shall be
those fixed and established by surveys ordered by the Council and thereafter
filed in the office of the City Clerk. When such surveys and profiles are
approved by the City Council and filed in the office of the City Clerk, they
establish the grades within their respective boundaries and with reference to
which all improvements shall conform.
(Prior Code, § 12.08.010)
   (B)   In the absence of the grade having been so established, it shall be
the duty of any person contemplating any improvement within the city to secure
a grade from the Street Commissioner.
(Prior Code, § 12.08.010)
(Ord. 192, passed - -1942)
§ 152.002 WATER FLOWING UPON STREETS.
   It is unlawful for any person to allow any water to flow into or upon any
public thoroughfare.
(Prior Code, § 12.24.030) Penalty, see §
152.999
§ 152.003 LUG WHEELS.
   It is unlawful for tractors with wheels injurious to pavement to be
permitted upon the public thoroughfares unless the operator of such vehicle
first planks such streets.
(Prior Code, § 12.24.040) Penalty, see §
152.999
§ 152.004 DEPOSITS OF INJURIOUS MATERIAL ON THOROUGHFARES.
   It is unlawful for any person to deposit, place or allow to remain in or
upon any public thoroughfare any material or substance injurious to person or
property.
(Prior Code, § 12.24.050) Penalty, see §
152.999
SIDEWALK CONSTRUCTION AND MAINTENANCE
§ 152.015 CITY COUNCIL AUTHORITY.
   The City Council may cause sidewalks to be built along any of the streets,
avenues or alleys, or other improvements to be made thereon, upon the same
being ordered by a majority of all the members of the Council, and the Council
shall have charge of the building, maintenance and repairs of all sidewalks of
whatever kind or character, and such work may be done by contract or by the
Street Commissioner, or other authorized officer of the city; provided,
however, that, any one or all kinds of sidewalks shall be built and maintained
at the cost of the owner of the property in front of which the sidewalk is
built or to be constructed.
(Prior Code, § 12.04.010) (Ord. 193, passed - -1942)
§ 152.016 COST ASSESSMENT.
   To defray the cost of constructing sidewalks and keeping the same in repair,
the Council shall assess the entire cost thereof to the property in front of
which the sidewalk is built. The property occupying a street corner is to be
assessed for that part of the sidewalk which is within the street intersection.
(Prior Code, § 12.04.020) (Ord. 193, passed - -1942)
§ 152.017 CONSTRUCTION SPECIFICATIONS FOR CERTAIN STREETS.
   All sidewalks which may be ordered by the City Council shall be constructed
under the supervision of the City Council, and out of concrete or cement
material, and shall be of the width specified as follows:
   (A)   Streets running east and west.
      (1)   Main Street from the west line of Lot 26 to and including the west
100 feet of Lot 37 in Block one of the original townsite of the city as laid
out by Elisha W. Tucker: ten feet wide;
      (2)   Front Street from the east line of Lot 7 in Block 3 of R.V.
Tucker’s first addition to the city to Seventh Avenue: ten feet wide; and
      (3)   Cosner Street, from Fourth Avenue to Seventh: ten feet wide.
   (B)   Streets or avenues running north and south. Fifth, Sixth and Seventh
Avenues from Front Street to Cosner Street: ten feet wide; and
   (C)   All other streets and avenues. All other streets and avenues: five
feet wide.
(Prior Code, § 12.04.030) (Ord. 193, passed - -1942)
§ 152.018 GRADES.
   The grades of all sidewalks shall be given by the Street Commissioner until
the permanent grade is established by the City Council.
(Prior Code, § 12.04.040) (Ord. 193, passed - -1942)
§ 152.019 OWNER’S DUTY TO KEEP SIDEWALKS SAFE FOR PEDESTRIANS; NON- COMPLIANCE.
   It shall be the duty of the occupant of any premises within the limits of
the city, or in case any such are unoccupied, then the owner or his or her
agent, to keep the sidewalk in front and adjoining his or her premises free and
safe for pedestrians and, with all reasonable dispatch, to remove snow, ice,
slush, mud or other impediment to safe and convenient foot travel, and prevent
the continuance and accumulation of same upon such sidewalks.
(Prior Code, § 12.04.050) (Ord. 193, passed - -1942) Penalty, see §
152.999
§ 152.020 RIDING ON SIDEWALK WITH VEHICLES AND THE LIKE PROHIBITED.
   It is unlawful for any person to ride or drive any horse, mule or other
animal, buggy, wagon, bicycle, automobile or other vehicle along or on any of
the sidewalks within the city.
(Prior Code, § 12.04.070) (Ord. 193, passed - -1942) Penalty, see §
152.999
§ 152.021 SIDEWALK CONSTRUCTION; WIDTH; SLOPE; CONFORMANCE TO EXISTING SIDEWALK
REQUIRED; NEW TYPE REQUIRED WHEN NO SIDEWALK PRESENT; CHANGE TO NEW TYPE;
APPLICATION REQUIRED.
   (A)   All sidewalks to be constructed in the city after 10-26-1964 shall be
of concrete and shall be five feet wide.
(Prior Code, § 12.04.090)
   (B)   All sidewalks constructed in the city after 10-26-1964, shall have a
slope towards the curb and gutter and such slope shall be one-quarter of an
inch to each foot of sidewalk width.
(Prior Code, § 12.04.100)
   (C)   (1)   If a sidewalk is presently located in a block in the city and an
owner of property in the block does not have a sidewalk located on his or her
property and he or she desires to build a sidewalk, the owner must build his or
her sidewalk to conform with the sidewalk presently existing in the block;
provided that, the existing sidewalk is of the width and has the slope provided
in divisions (A) and (B) above.
      (2)   However, the owner may make application to the governing body of
the city to construct a “new type” sidewalk, namely a sidewalk adjoining the
curb, on a block on which an “old type” sidewalk, namely a sidewalk which does
not adjoin the curb, is located and upon receiving such approval shall install
such “new type” sidewalk in accordance with divisions (A) and (B) above and
shall connect such sidewalk to any existing sidewalks as is required by the
governing body in its approval of the application.
(Prior Code, § 12.04.110)
   (D)   If there is no sidewalk presently built in a block in the city and
owners of property in the block desire to build sidewalks, such sidewalks must
be of the “new type”; namely, they must be constructed adjacent to and must
join the curb located in the block and must be of the slope and width as
provided in divisions (A) and (B) above.
(Prior Code, § 12.04.120)
   (E)   If there are sidewalks located in a block in the city and any or all
of the owners of property in the block desire to change the construction of the
sidewalk to the “new type”; namely, sidewalk adjoining the curb, the owner or
owners must make application to the governing body of the city for the change
of sidewalk and upon receiving approval of the governing body for the change,
the old sidewalk must be removed and a new sidewalk constructed in accordance
with the provisions of divisions (A) and (B) above and shall be connected to
any existing sidewalks as shall be required by the governing body in its
approval of the application.
(Prior Code, § 12.04.130)
(Ord. 276, passed - -1964; Ord. 376, passed - -1990)
STREET AND ALLEY EXCAVATIONS
§ 152.035 PERMIT REQUIRED.
   It is unlawful for any person, persons, firm or corporation to cut through
or tear open any surface of any street within the city without first applying
for and obtaining a permit to do so in accordance with the provisions contained
in this subhapter.
(Prior Code, § 12.12.010) (Ord. 385, passed - -1991) Penalty, see §
152.999
§ 152.036 PERMIT APPLICATION; CONTENTS.
   Any person, persons, firm or corporation desiring to cut through or tear
open the surface of any street or alley within the city shall first file a
written application said application shall state the objects sought, the
purpose for which the street or alley is to be cut or broken open, the proposed
area of such opening and the exact location thereof.
(Prior Code, § 12.12.020) (Ord. 385, passed - -1991)
§ 152.037 OPENINGS LESS THAN 1,000 SQUARE FEET.
   (A)   (1)   If the opening or openings proposed in such application do not
exceed 1,000 square feet, the Director of Public Works or authorized
representative may, in his or her discretion, grant or refuse to grant a permit
for such work.
      (2)   The refusal of the Director of Public Works or authorized
representative to grant any such permission is subject to review by the City
Council.
   (B)   (1)   In case a permit is granted to the applicant, the applicant
shall accomplish the proposed work within the time allowed by the Director of
Public Works or authorized representative and under his or her supervision and
shall backfill any such excavation by tamping in six-inch lifts.
      (2)   In the event the proposed opening is in pavement, the surface shall
be left in such condition so that the city may repair the pavement by repaving
the opening.
      (3)   No tunneling shall be allowed under any street or alley within the
city for a distance greater than 15 feet without providing at least one opening
to the surface thereof for backfilling. Backfill shall be thoroughly tamped in
layers to prevent settlement.
      (4)   Within a reasonable time after the backfilling has been completed
in any excavation made in a paved street, the city shall restore the surface
thereof.
      (5)   All alley excavation shall be the responsibility of the person,
persons, firm or corporation to backfill and tamp as required in this section.
      (6)   All street or alley openings are to be inspected by the Director of
Public Works or an authorized representative of the city.
(Prior Code, § 12.12.030) (Ord. 385, passed - -1991) Penalty, see §
152.999
§ 152.038 OPENINGS GREATER THAN 1,000 SQUARE FEET.
   (A)   Where the opening or openings proposed in such application exceed
1,000 square feet, the applicant must appear before the City Council for
permission to open the street, streets, alley or alleys and must pay for such
work as provided in §
152.039 of this chapter.
   (B)   Where separate applications are made covering one continuous project,
immediately under construction, the total area included in all of the
applications shall be the basis for determining the amount to be paid.
(Prior Code, § 12.12.040) (Ord. 385, passed - -1991)
§ 152.039 CHARGES.
   The charges to be made for street and alley openings of any kind or
character whatsoever shall be set by resolution.
(Prior Code, § 12.12.050) (Ord. 385, passed - -1991; Ord. 392, passed - -1994)
§ 152.040 BOND REQUIRED.
   Any contractor, plumber, property owner or other person, persons, firm or
corporation applying for permission to open any street or alley must post, with
the City Clerk, a bond in the penal sum of $1,500 payable to the city to
protect the city from any liability of any kind or character whatsoever, which
may arise, as a result of the applicant’s opening any such street or alley, or
which may be in any way or manner connected therewith or related thereto.
(Prior Code, § 12.12.060) (Ord. 385, passed - -1991)
§ 152.041 PUBLIC LIABILITY AND PROPERTY DAMAGE INSURANCE REQUIRED.
   Before any permit to open any public way is granted, the applicant for such
permit shall furnish satisfactory evidence that there has been issued to the
applicant, and is in full force and effect, public liability insurance in the
amount not less than $25,000 for injuries, including accidental death to any
one person and subject to the same limit for each person, in an amount not less
than $50,000 on account of one accident and property damage insurance in an
amount not less than $10,000 with indemnity endorsement for the protection of
the city.
(Prior Code, § 12.12.070) (Ord. 385, passed - -1991)
§ 152.042 PERMITTEE’S RESPONSIBILITY.
   The permittee in accepting and acting under a street or alley opening permit
granted under the provisions of this subchapter thereby agrees to assume full
responsibility for injury to persons or losses or damage to property incurred
by reason of or arising out of any act or omission of such permittee in making
such excavation, cut or opening or in failing properly to barricade, guard and
warn the public of such excavation or trench and, further, thereby agrees to
assume full responsibility for any injury to persons or losses or damage to
property incurred by reason of or arising out of any settlement of a restored
area occurring within one year of the date of completion of the permanent
resurfacing.
(Prior Code, § 12.12.080) (Ord. 385, passed - -1991) Penalty, see §
152.999
§ 152.043 SETTLEMENT A LIABILITY OF PERMITTEE.
   (A)   If any settlement in any restored area occurs within one year of the
date of completion of the permanent surfacing, it shall be considered as
conclusive evidence of defective backfill.
   (B)   Upon failure or refusal of such permittee to correct such settlement
within five days after notice by the Director of Public Works to do so, any
expense incurred by the city in correcting such settlement shall be paid by the
permittee.
(Prior Code, § 12.12.090) (Ord. 385, passed - -1991)
§ 152.044 TO IMPEDE TRAFFIC AS LITTLE AS POSSIBLE.
   Permitted excavations in streets, avenues and alleys shall be made in such
manner so as to impede travel thereon as little as possible.
(Prior Code, § 12.12.100) (Ord. 385, passed - -1991) Penalty, see §
152.999
§ 152.045 TIME LIMIT.
   (A)   The time that any street, avenue or alley permitted excavation is open
may be limited by the Director of Public Works or his or her assistant or
inspector.
   (B)   At no time during the progress of the work shall sidewalks be
unnecessarily blocked to travel.
(Prior Code, § 12.12.110) (Ord. 385, passed - -1991) Penalty, see §
152.999
§ 152.046 BARRICADES.
   Sufficient barricades to permitted excavations on streets, avenues and
alleys shall be erected by the contractor doing the excavation work under
permit around all trenches or embankments made by him or her within the limits
of any street, avenue or alley and red lights shall be maintained thereon from
dark until daylight until the street, avenue or alley shall be restored to safe
and passable condition.
(Prior Code, § 12.12.120) (Ord. 385, passed - -1991)
STREET MAINTENANCE
§ 152.060 STREET MAINTENANCE DISTRICT CREATED.
   There is created within the city a street maintenance district for the
maintenance of all streets and avenues in the city.
(Prior Code, § 12.28.010) (Ord. 339, passed - -1983)
§ 152.061 PERFORMANCE OF MAINTENANCE WORK.
   Street maintenance work shall be done as follows: the maintenance work may
be done by contract or by forces employed by the city, or both, in such manner
as the City Council may elect.
(Prior Code, § 12.28.020) (Ord. 339, passed - -1983)
§ 152.062 PAYMENT FOR MAINTENANCE WORK.
   (A)   Such maintenance work shall be paid for as follows: assessment of
costs of maintaining streets, alleys and public places shall be made against
all of the property embraced within a maintenance district and shall be made
and computed as follows: each lot or parcel of land within a maintenance
district abutting upon a street upon which maintenance is done shall be
assessed for that part of the whole cost which its street frontage bears to the
street frontage of the entire district.
   (B)   Corner lots will be assessed on the basis of the narrower dimension of
such corner lots abutting upon a street upon which maintenance is done.
(Prior Code, § 12.28.030) (Ord. 339, passed - -1983)
§ 152.063 “MAINTENANCE” DEFINED.
   MAINTENANCE, as used in this subchapter, includes, but is not limited to,
sprinkling, graveling, oiling, chip sealing, seal coating, overlaying,
treating, general cleaning, sweeping, flushing, snow removal and leaf and
debris removal.
(Prior Code, § 12.28.040) (Ord. 339, passed - -1983)
PUBLIC SKATEPARK
§ 152.075 ESTABLISHED.
   The city has established and maintained a public skatepark located at
Hillcrest Park on South 12th Street East in the Hillcrest Subdivision, Malta,
Montana. Said described land shall be used as a public skatepark for the city.
(Prior Code, § 12.32.010) (Ord. 446, passed - -2016)
§ 152.076 MANAGEMENT.
   The local officials, including, but not limited to, the Mayor and law
enforcement, of the city shall be responsible for the control and management of
the public skatepark, subject to the rules and conditions contained herein, and
subject to revisions made by the City Council.
(Prior Code, § 12.32.020) (Ord. 446, passed - -2016)
§ 152.077 SKATEPARK RULES AND REGULATIONS.
   It is unlawful for any person to violate any of the following rules and
regulations while at the skatepark.
   (A)   Use of the facility is only allowed during park hours (dawn to dusk).
After hours use or use when closed will result in a trespass citation.
   (B)   All persons within the skatepark area must be alert and exercise
common sense and courtesy to others. Skateparks are prone to flying objects and
bodies. Know individual abilities and skate within them.
   (C)   Proper use of protective gear (helmets, wrist guards, elbow and knee
pads) is strongly recommended. Concrete and steel are harder than an individual
is.
   (D)   Skateboards and in-line skates and kids’ scooters only. Absolutely no
bicycles or motor vehicles. Violations will result in trespass citations and
possible seizure of equipment.
   (E)   No obstacles, other material, glass, food or drink is allowed in the
skatepark. These items jeopardize the skaters.
   (F)   Do not skate if the surface is wet or icy. The skatepark surface is
extremely dangerous when wet.
   (G)   No spectators inside the skating area. Spectators, please watch from
outside the facility; it will be much safer there.
   (H)   Trash containers must be used to keep the park clean and safe. Help
keep the skatepark clean. Use the trash cans; “you pack it in you pack it out”.
   (I)   Be considerate of the surrounding property and neighbors by skating
only in the skatepark area. No loud music.
   (J)   Alcohol, tobacco products, drugs and offensive language are
prohibited.
(Prior Code, § 12.32.030) (Ord. 446, passed - -2016) Penalty, see §
152.999
§ 152.999 PENALTY.
   (A)   Any person violating any provision of this chapter for which no
specific penalty is prescribed shall be subject to §
10.99 of this code of ordinances.
   (B)   (1)   (a)   If any person assists in building or builds any sidewalks
where no grade has been established without first obtaining a grade therefor
from the Street Commissioner, or contrary to any grade which may have been
established by the City Council, or contrary to any of the provisions of §§
152.015 through
152.020 of this chapter, he or she shall in such case be subject to a penalty
of $10 for every offense, and to a like penalty for every day he or she fails
to remove or reconstruct the same.
(Prior Code, § 12.04.040)
         (b)   The penalty for the violation of any of the provisions of §§
152.015 through
152.020 of this chapter, when the same is not specifically mentioned, shall be
not less than $10, nor more than $50, for each offense.
(Prior Code, § 12.04.080)
      (2)   Every person failing to comply with the requirements of §
152.019 of this chapter shall be guilty of committing a nuisance and, upon
conviction thereof, shall be fined not less than $5, nor more than $50, and
after having been notified by the Chief of Police to remove the same, and
failing to do so within a reasonable time thereafter, such person so offending
shall be guilty of a separate offense for each 24 hours the same remains so
unremoved, and subject to a like penalty as provided in this division (B)(2)
for each separate violation.
(Prior Code, § 12.04.060)
      (3)   Any person or persons guilty of violating any of the provisions of
§
152.020 of this chapter shall be fined in any sum not less than $10, nor more
than $50, and the costs of prosecution.
(Prior Code, § 12.04.070)
   (C)   Violations of §§
152.035 through
152.046 of this chapter shall be punished by a fine of not to exceed $100 or by
imprisonment in the city jail for a period of not exceeding 50 days or by both
such fine and imprisonment.
(Prior Code, § 12.12.130)
   (D)   Any person violating any of the provisions of §§
152.075 through
152.077 of this chapter shall, upon conviction before a court of competent
jurisdiction, be guilty of an offense, and shall be subject to the general
penalty provisions of this code and applicable state law as may be appropriate.
(Prior Code, § 12.32.040)
(Ord. 193, passed - -1942; Ord. 385, passed - -1991; Ord. 446, passed - -2016)

§ 153.01 TREE TRIMMING REQUIRED.
   Any owner or occupant of any real property shall trim all trees on property
owned or occupied by him or her overhanging any public thoroughfare, so that
the branches thereon will not interfere with pedestrians or public travel.
(Prior Code, § 12.16.010) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 153.02 HEDGE AND SHRUBBERY MAINTENANCE REQUIRED.
   Any owner or occupant of any real property shall maintain all hedges and
shrubbery adjacent to public sidewalks so that no part of said hedges and/or
shrubbery shall extend over any part of a public sidewalk in the city.
(Prior Code, § 12.16.020) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 153.03 INJURY TO TREES OR SHRUBBERY PROHIBITED.
   It is unlawful for any person, not the owner thereof, or without lawful
authority to do so, willfully to injure, deface, disfigure or destroy any tree
or shrub, or to injure, destroy, cut or pick any flower or plant, located
either on private ground or on any public place or thoroughfare.
(Prior Code, § 12.16.030) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 153.04 CONTROL OVER TREES OUTSIDE OF PRIVATE PROPERTY LINES.
   The governing body of the city is provided full and complete control over
all trees which are outside the property lines of privately-owned real estate.
(Prior Code, § 12.16.040)

GENERAL PROVISIONS
§ 154.001 FLOODPLAIN HAZARD MANAGEMENT REGULATIONS.
   These regulations are known and may be cited as the “Floodplain Hazard
Management Regulations”, hereinafter referred to as “these regulations”.
(Prior Code, § 15.52.010) (Ord. 455, passed 11-23-2021)
§ 154.002 STATUTORY AUTHORITY.
   (A)   Floodplain and floodway management is incorporated in M.C.A. Title 76,
Chapter 5, and describes the authority, procedures and minimum standards for
local regulations and is further described in A.R.M. Chapter 36.15.
   (B)   The authority to regulate development in specifically identified flood
hazard areas has been accepted pursuant to M.C.A. § 76-5-301.
(Prior Code, § 15.52.020) (Ord. 455, passed 11-23-2021)
§ 154.003 FINDINGS OF FACT.
   (A)   Flood hazard areas specifically adopted herein as regulated flood
hazard areas have been delineated and designated by order or determination of
the Department of Natural Resources and Conservation (DNRC) pursuant to M.C.A.
§§ 76-5-201 et seq.
   (B)   (1)   These regulations have been reviewed by the state’s Department
of Natural Resources and Conservation and the Federal Emergency Management
Agency.
      (2)   The state’s Department of Natural Resources and Conservation has
found the regulations acceptable in meeting the Department minimum standards.
      (3)   The Federal Emergency Management Agency finds that these
regulations are adequate and consistent with the comprehensive criteria for
land management and use pursuant to the standards established in 44 C.F.R. §
60.3.
(A.R.M. § 36.15.202) (M.C.A. § 76-5-302) (44 C.F.R. § 60.1(b)) (42 U.S.C. §
4022) (Prior Code, § 15.52.030) (Ord. 455, passed 11-23-2021)
§ 154.004 PURPOSE.
   (A)   The purpose of these regulations is to promote public health, safety
and general welfare of the residents and minimize public and private losses due
to flood conditions in regulated flood hazard areas.
   (B)   These regulations are intended to:
      (1)   Protect human life and health;
      (2)   Minimize expenditure of public money for costly flood control
projects;
      (3)   Minimize the need for rescue and relief efforts associated with
flooding and generally undertaken at the expense of the general public;
      (4)   Minimize prolonged business and public service interruptions;
      (5)   Minimize damage to public facilities and utilities such as water
and gas mains, electric, telephone and sewer lines, streets and bridges;
      (6)   Help maintain a stable tax base by providing for the sound use and
development of flood-prone areas in such a manner as to minimize future flood
disruptions; and
      (7)   Ensure compliance with the minimum standards for the continued
participation in the National Flood Insurance Program for the benefit of the
residents.
(Prior Code, § 15.52.040) (Ord. 455, passed 11-23-2021)
§ 154.005 METHODS TO REDUCE LOSSES.
   In accordance with M.C.A. § 76-5-102, these regulations are intended to
reduce flood losses through the following methods:
   (A)   Restrict or prohibit uses that are dangerous to health, safety or
property in times of flooding or that may cause excessive increases in flood
heights or velocities;
   (B)   Require that uses of land vulnerable to floods, including public
facilities, be developed or constructed to at least minimum standards or to
otherwise minimize flood damage;
   (C)   Regulate the alteration of natural floodplains, stream channels and
natural protective barriers which are needed to accommodate flood waters;
   (D)   Regulate filling, grading, dredging and other development which may
increase flood damage;
   (E)   Prevent or regulate the construction of flood barriers which will
impact other land, flood water depth or velocity of flood waters;
   (F)   Distinguish between the land use regulations applied to the floodway
within the regulated flood hazard area and those applied to that portion of the
regulated flood hazard area not contained in the floodway;
   (G)   Apply more restrictive land use regulations within the floodway of the
regulated flood hazard area; and
   (H)   Ensure that regulations and minimum standards balance the greatest
public good with the least private injury.
(Prior Code, § 15.52.050) (Ord. 455, passed 11-23-2021)
§ 154.006 REGULATED AREA.
   (A)   These regulations apply only to the flood hazard areas specifically
adopted herein as regulated flood hazard areas which are more fully and
specifically described in §§
154.035 through
154.039 of this chapter. Requirements and approvals for alterations to the
regulated flood hazard area are specified in §§
154.035 through
154.039 of this chapter. The regulated flood hazard area includes areas
specifically identified, labeled and illustrated on maps such as floodplain,
floodway or flood fringe that have differing uses allowed and minimum building
standards that apply. The regulated flood hazard area is the geographic area
inundated by the flood of 100-year frequency illustrated and depicted in the
referenced studies and maps.
   (B)   The regulated flood hazard area supporting study and maps illustrating
the regulatory area are based on studies and maps that have been specifically
adopted pursuant to M.C.A. §§ 76-5-201 et seq. The maps and accompanying study
become the regulated flood hazard area only when formally adopted by DNRC and
subsequently by the political subdivision by these regulations. The original
source of studies and data may be from a Flood Insurance Study by FEMA, or
other studies by Corps of Engineers, Soil Conservation, United States
Geological Service or other federal or state agency.
(Prior Code, § 15.52.060) (Ord. 455, passed 11-23-2021)
§ 154.007 FLOODPLAIN ADMINISTRATOR.
   A Floodplain Administrator is hereby officially appointed and is the
responsibility of the Office of the City Clerk-Treasurer. The Floodplain
Administrator’s duty is to administer and implement the provisions of these
regulations. The Floodplain Administrator must serve to meet and maintain the
commitments pursuant to 44 C.F.R. § 59.22(a) to FEMA to remain eligible for
national flood insurance for individuals and business within the political
subdivision.
(A.R.M. § 36.15.204(2)(h)) (44 C.F.R. § 59.22(b)(1)) (Prior Code, § 15.52.070)
(Ord. 455, passed 11-23- 2021)
§ 154.008 COMPLIANCE.
   Development, new construction, alteration or substantial improvement may not
commence without full compliance with the provisions of these regulations.
(Prior Code, § 15.52.080) (Ord. 455, passed 11-23-2021)
§ 154.009 ABROGATION AND GREATER RESPONSIBILITY.
   It is not intended by these regulations to repeal, abrogate or impair any
existing easements, covenants, deed restrictions, zoning or other regulations
in effect. However, where these regulations impose greater restrictions, the
provision of these regulations must prevail.
(44 C.F.R. § 60.1(d)) (Prior Code, § 15.52.090) (Ord. 455, passed 11-23-2021)
§ 154.010 REGULATION INTERPRETATION.
   In the interpretation and application of these regulations, all provisions
shall be:
   (A)   Considered as minimum requirements;
   (B)   Liberally construed in favor of the governing body; and
   (C)   Deemed neither to limit, nor repeal, any other powers granted under
state statutes.
(44 C.F.R. § 60.1) (Prior Code, § 15.52.100) (Ord. 455, passed 11-23-2021)
§ 154.011 WARNING AND DISCLAIMER OF LIABILITY.
   These regulations do not imply that land outside the regulated flood hazard
areas or uses permitted within such areas will be free from flooding or flood
damages. These regulations shall not create liability on the part of the
community or any official or employee thereof for any flood damages that result
from reliance on these regulations or any administrative decision lawfully made
hereunder.
(Prior Code, § 15.52.110) (Ord. 455, passed 11-23-2021)
§ 154.012 SEVERABILITY.
   If any section, clause, sentence or phrase of these regulations is held to
be invalid or unconstitutional by any court of competent jurisdiction, then
said holding will in no way affect the validity of the remaining portions of
these regulations.
(Prior Code, § 15.52.120) (Ord. 455, passed 11-23-2021)
§ 154.013 DISCLOSURE PROVISION.
   All property owners or their agents in the regulated flood hazard areas
shall notify potential buyers or their agents that such property, including any
permitted uses transferred, is located within the regulated flood hazard area
and is subject to regulation and any permitted uses that are transferred.
Information regarding regulated flood hazard area and the repository for
floodplain maps is available in the Floodplain Administrator’s office.
(A.R.M. § 36.15.204(2)(g)) (Prior Code, § 15.52.130) (Ord. 455, passed 11-23-
2021)
§ 154.014 AMENDMENT OF REGULATIONS.
   (A)   These regulations may be amended after notice and public hearing in
regard to the amendments to these regulations.
   (B)   The amendments must be found adequate and acceptable by DNRC and FEMA
to be effective and must be submitted for review at least 30 days prior to
official adoption.
(Prior Code, § 15.52.140) (Ord. 455, passed 11-23-2021)
§ 154.015 PUBLIC RECORDS.
   Records, including permits and applications, elevation and flood proofing
certificates, certificates of compliance, fee receipts and other matters
relating to these regulations must be maintained by the Floodplain
Administrator and are public records and must be made available for inspection
and for copies upon reasonable request. A reasonable copying cost for copying
documents for members of the public may be charged and may require payments of
the costs before providing the copies.
(44 C.F.R. §§ 59.22(a)(9)(iii), 60.3(b)(5)(iii)) (Prior Code, § 15.52.150)
(Ord. 455, passed 11-23-2021)
§ 154.016 SUBDIVISION REVIEW.
   Within the regulated flood hazard area, subdivisions including new or
expansion of existing manufactured home parks, must be designed to meet the
following criteria:
   (A)   The base flood elevations and boundary of the regulated flood hazard
area must be determined and considered during lot layout and building location
design;
   (B)   Locations for future structures and development must be reasonably
safe from flooding;
(44 C.F.R. § 60.3(a)(4))
   (C)   Adequate surface water drainage must be provided to reduce exposure to
flood hazards;
(44 C.F.R. § 60.3(a)(4)(iii))
   (D)   Public utilities and facilities such as sewer, gas, electrical and
water systems must be located and constructed to minimize or eliminate flood
damage; and
(44 C.F.R. § 60.3(a)(4)(ii))
   (E)   Floodplain permits must be obtained according to these regulations
before development occurs that is within the regulated flood hazard area.
(44 C.F.R. § 60.3(b))
(Prior Code, § 15.52.160) (Ord. 455, passed 11-23-2021)
§ 154.017 DISASTER RECOVERY.
   (A)   In the event of a natural or human-made disaster, the Floodplain
Administrator should participate in the coordination of assistance and provide
information to structure owners concerning hazard mitigation and recovery
measures with the Federal Emergency Management Agency, the state’s Disaster
Emergency Services, the state’s Department of Natural Resources and
Conservation and other state, local and private emergency service
organizations.
   (B)   Upon completion of cursory street view structure condition survey
within the regulated flood hazard area, the Floodplain Administrator shall
notify owners that a permit may be necessary for an alteration or substantial
improvement before repair or reconstruction commences on damaged structures
because of damages caused by natural or human-made disasters such as floods,
fires or winds.
   (C)   Owners should be advised that structures that have suffered
substantial damage and will undergo substantial improvements require a
floodplain application and permit and must be upgraded to meet the minimum
building standards herein during repair or reconstruction.
(A.R.M. § 36.15.702) (M.C.A. § 76-5-404(3)(b)) (44 C.F.R. § 60.3(c)(2) and I.C.
(3)) (Prior Code, § 15.52.170) (Ord. 455, passed 11-23-2021)
§ 154.018 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this chapter, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   100-YEAR FLOOD. A 1% annual chance flood. See also definition of base flood.
   ALTERATION. Any change or addition to an artificial obstruction that either
increases its external dimensions or increases its potential flood hazard.
(A.R.M. § 36.15.101(2))
   APPURTENANT STRUCTURE. A structure in which the use is incidental or
accessory to the use of a principal structure.
(44 C.F.R. § 59.1)
   ARTIFICIAL OBSTRUCTION. Any obstruction which is not natural and includes
any development, dam, diversion, wall, riprap, embankment, levee, dike, pile,
abutment, projection, revetment, excavation, channel rectification, road,
bridge, conduit, culvert, building, refuse, automobile body, fill or other
analogous structure or matter in, along, across or projecting into any
regulated flood hazard area that may impede, retard or change the direction of
the flow of water, either in itself or by catching or collecting debris carried
by the water, or that is placed where the natural flow of the water would carry
the same downstream to the damage or detriment of either life or property. See
also definition of development.
(A.R.M. § 36.15.101(3)) (M.C.A. § 76-5-103(1))
   BASE FLOOD (FLOOD OF 100-YEAR FREQUENCY). A flood having a 1% chance of
being equaled or exceeded in any given year.
(A.R.M. § 36.15.101(4)) (44 C.F.R. § 59.1)
   BASE FLOOD ELEVATION (BFE). The elevation above sea level of the base flood
in relation to the National Geodetic Vertical Datum of 1929 or the North
American Vertical Datum of 1988 or unless otherwise specified.
(A.R.M. § 36.15.101(5))
   BASEMENT. Any area of a building, except a crawl space, as having its lowest
floor below ground level on all sides.
(44 C.F.R. § 59.1) (NFIP Insurance Manual, Rev. May 2013)
   BUILDING. A walled and roofed structure, including a gas or liquid storage
tank that is principally above ground, as well as a manufactured home.
(44 C.F.R. § 59.1)
   CHANNEL. The geographical area within either the natural or artificial banks
of a watercourse or drain way.
(M.C.A. § 76-5-103(2))
   CRAWL SPACE. An enclosure that has its interior floor area no more than five
feet below the top of the next highest floor. See definitions of enclosure and
subgrade crawlspace.
(NFIP Insurance Manual, Rev. May 2013)
   DNRC. Montana Department of Natural Resources and Conservation.
   DEVELOPMENT. Any human-made change to improved or unimproved real estate,
including, but not limited to, buildings or other structures, mining, dredging,
filling, grading, paving, excavation or drilling operations or storage of
equipment or materials. See also definition of ARTIFICIAL OBSTRUCTION.
(44 C.F.R. § 59.1)
   ELEVATED BUILDING. A building that has no basement and that has its lowest
elevated floor raised above ground level by foundation walls, shear walls,
posts, piers, pilings or columns. A building on a crawlspace is considered an
ELEVATED BUILDING.
(NFIP Insurance Manual, Rev. May 2013)
   ENCLOSURE. That portion below the lowest elevated floor of an elevated
building that is either partially or fully shut in by rigid walls including a
crawlspace, sub grade crawlspace, stairwell, elevator or a garage below or
attached.
   ENCROACHMENT. Activities or construction within the regulated flood hazard
area including fill, new construction, substantial improvements and other
development.
   ENCROACHMENT ANALYSIS. A hydrologic and hydraulic analysis performed by an
engineer to assess the effects of the proposed artificial obstruction or non-
conforming use on base flood elevation, flood flows and flood velocities.
   ESTABLISH. To construct, place, insert or excavate.
(A.R.M. § 36.15.101(9)) (M.C.A. § 76-5-103(7))
   EXISTING ARTIFICIAL OBSTRUCTION OR NON-CONFORMING USE. An artificial
obstruction or non-conforming use that was established before land use
regulations were adopted pursuant to M.C.A. § 76-5-404(3).
   FEMA. Federal Emergency Management Agency.
   FLOOD FRINGE. The identified portion of the floodplain of the regulated
flood hazard area outside the limits of the floodway.
(A.R.M. § 36.15.101(10))
   FLOOD OF 100-YEAR FREQUENCY (BASE FLOOD). A flood magnitude expected to
recur on the average of once every 100 years or a flood magnitude that has a 1%
chance of occurring in any given year.
(44 C.F.R. § 59.1) (M.C.A. § 76-5-103(9))
   FLOOD-PROOFING. Any combination of structural and non-structural additions,
changes or adjustments to structures which reduce or eliminate flood damage to
real estate or improved real property, water and sanitary facilities,
electrical, plumbing, HVAC systems, structures and their contents. The term
includes wet flood-proofing, dry flood-proofing and elevation of structures.
(44 C.F.R. § 59.1)
   FLOODPLAIN. The area of the regulated flood hazard area including and
adjoining the watercourse or drainway that would be covered by the flood water
of a base flood. The area is partitioned into a flood fringe and floodway where
specifically designated. See definition of REGULATED FLOOD HAZARD AREA.
   FLOODPLAIN ADMINISTRATOR. Community official or representative appointed to
administer and implement the provisions of this chapter.
   FLOODWAY. The identified portion of the floodplain of the regulated flood
hazard area that is the channel and the area adjoining the channel that is
reasonably required to carry the discharge of the base flood without
cumulatively increasing the water surface by more than one-half foot.
(M.C.A. §§ 76-5-103(5), 76-5-103(11))
   LETTER OF MAP CHANGE (LOMC). An official response from FEMA that amends or
revises the FEMA special flood hazard area and FEMA Flood Insurance Study for
flood insurance purposes and/or flood risk hazard. FEMA LETTERS OF MAP CHANGE
specific to an amendment or revision include the following.
      (1)   CONDITIONAL LETTER OF MAP REVISION (CLOMR). A FEMA letter of
approval for a proposed physical change that when completed would propose to
change the flood zones, delineation or elevations on the FEMA Flood Insurance
Rate Map or FEMA Flood Boundary Map and may amend the FEMA Flood Insurance
Study through a subsequent LOMR. The CLOMR may be considered in an evaluation
by DNRC and the Floodplain Administrator during consideration of a proposed
alteration to the regulated flood hazard area.
      (2)   LETTER OF MAP AMENDMENT (LOMA). A letter of determination from FEMA
issued in response to a request that a property or structure is not subject to
the mandatory flood insurance requirement because it was inadvertently located
in the effective FEMA special flood hazard area. The material submitted and
response from FEMA may be considered by the Floodplain Administrator for
determining if a property or structure is within the regulated flood hazard
area and subject to these regulations.
      (3)   LETTER OF MAP REVISION (LOMR). An official FEMA amendment to the
currently effective FEMA Flood Insurance Rate Map or FEMA Flood Boundary Map
based on a physical change to the floodplain of the special flood hazard area.
It is issued by FEMA and changes flood zones, delineations and elevations on
the FEMA Flood Insurance Rate Map or FEMA Flood Boundary Map and may amend the
FEMA Flood Insurance Study. It must be preceded by an approved alteration of
the designated floodplain from DNRC and subsequently an amendment to the
regulated flood hazard area.
      (4)   LETTER OF MAP REVISION BASED ON FILL (LOMR-F). A letter of approval
from FEMA removing the mandatory requirement for flood insurance on property
based on placement of fill or an addition. Placement of fill or an addition
must be preceded by a permit pursuant to these regulations. Placement of fill
does not remove the development from the regulated flood hazard area or these
regulations.
   LOWEST FLOOR.
      (1)   Any floor of a building including a basement used for living
purposes, storage or recreation.
      (2)   This includes any floor that could be converted to such a use.
(A.R.M. § 36.15.101(14)) (44 C.F.R. § 59.1)
   MANUFACTURED HOME PARK OR SUBDIVISION. Includes the construction of
facilities for servicing the manufactured home lots and at a minimum includes
the installation of utilities, the construction of streets and either final
site grading or the pouring of concrete pads.
(44 C.F.R. § 59.1)
   MANUFACTURED OR MOBILE HOME. A building that may be residential or non-
residential, is transportable in one or more sections, built on a permanent
chassis and designed to be used with or without a permanent foundation when
connected to the required utilities and includes park trailers, travel trailers
and other similar vehicles placed on a site for greater than 180 consecutive
days.
(A.R.M. § 36.15.101(15))
   NEW CONSTRUCTION. Structures for which the commencement of clearing,
grading, filling or excavating to prepare a site for construction occurs on or
after the effective date of these regulations and includes any subsequent
improvements to such structures.
(A.R.M. § 36.15.101(20)) (44 C.F.R. § 59.1)
   NEW MANUFACTURED HOME PARK OR SUBDIVISION. A manufactured home park or
subdivision for which the construction of facilities for servicing the lots on
which the manufactured homes are to be affixed includes at a minimum, the
installation of utilities, the construction of streets and either final site
grading or the pouring of concrete pads and is completed on or after the
effective date of floodplain management regulations adopted by a community.
(44 C.F.R. § 59.1)
   NON-RESIDENTIAL. Buildings including manufactured homes that are not
residential including commercial, agricultural, industrial buildings and
accessory buildings. See definition of RESIDENTIAL BUILDING.
   OWNER. Any person who has dominion over, control of or title to an
artificial obstruction.
(M.C.A. § 76-5-103(13))
   PERSON. Includes any individual, or group of individuals, corporation,
partnership, association or any other entity, including state and local
governments and agencies.
(44 C.F.R. § 59.1)
   RECREATIONAL VEHICLE. A park trailer, travel trailer or other similar
vehicle which is:
      (1)   Built on a single chassis;
      (2)   Four hundred square feet or less when measured at the largest
horizontal projections;
      (3)   Designed to be self-propelled or permanently towable by a motorized
vehicle; and
      (4)   Designed primarily for use as temporary living quarters for
recreation, camping, travel or seasonal use, not for use as a permanent
dwelling.
(44 C.F.R. § 59.1)
   REGULATED FLOOD HAZARD AREA. A floodplain whose limits have been designated
pursuant to M.C.A. Title 76, Chapter 5, part 2, and is determined to be the
area adjoining the watercourse that would be covered by the flood water of a
base flood. The REGULATED FLOOD HAZARD AREA consists of the floodway and flood
fringe where specifically designated.
(A.R.M. § 36-15-101(11)) (M.C.A. §§ 76-5-103(4), 76-5-103(10))
   RESIDENTIAL BUILDING. A dwelling or building for living purposes or place of
assembly or permanent use by human beings and including any mixed use of
residential and non-residential use. All other buildings are non-residential.
   RIPRAP. Stone, rocks, concrete blocks or analogous materials that are placed
along the bed or banks of a watercourse or drainway for the purpose of
preventing or alleviating erosion.
(A.R.M. § 36.15.101(18))
   SCOUR DEPTH. The maximum depth of streambed scour caused by erosive forces
of the base flood.
   SPECIAL FLOOD HAZARD AREA. Land area which has been specifically identified
by the Federal Emergency Management Agency as the floodplain within a community
subject to a 1% or greater chance of flooding in any given year. It is useful
for the purposes of identifying flood hazards by local subdivisions of
government for regulatory purposes as well as use by the National Flood
Insurance Program for establishing risk zones and flood insurance premium
rates. The FEMA flood hazard area zone designation or flood risk potential is
as illustrated on FEMA’s Flood Hazard Boundary Map or Flood Insurance Rate Map.
   STRUCTURE. Any artificial obstruction.
   SUBGRADE CRAWLSPACE. A crawlspace foundation enclosure that has its interior
floor no more than five feet below the top of the next higher floor and no more
than two feet below the lowest adjacent grade on all sides. A foundation
exceeding either dimension is a basement.
(NFIP Insurance Manual, Rev. May 2013)
   SUBSTANTIAL DAMAGE. Damage of any origin sustained by a structure whereby
the cost of restoring the structure to its before-damaged condition would
exceed 50% of the market value of the structure before the damage occurred.
(44 C.F.R. § 59.1)
