   (I)   The bench sign permit may be revoked at any time for lack of adequate
maintenance or other sufficient cause, after which the bench sign shall be
removed by the sign owner within seven days. If the owner fails to remove the
sign, the city may remove the sign, which shall become the property of the
city. The sign owner may reclaim the sign by paying removal costs, plus a $25
fee.
(Prior Code, § 15.68.020) (Ord. 392A, passed - -1994)

GENERAL PROVISIONS
§ 156.001 TITLE.
   This chapter shall be known and cited as the “Zoning Ordinance of the City
of Malta, Montana”.
(Prior Code, § 17.04.010) (Ord. 390, passed - -1993)
§ 156.002 PURPOSE.
   The purpose of this chapter is to promulgate and adopt such regulations as
necessary to comply with the Comprehensive Plan designed to lessen congestion
in the streets; to secure safety from fire, panic and other dangers; to promote
health and the general welfare; to provide adequate light and air; to prevent
overcrowding of land; and to avoid undue concentration of population; to
facilitate the adequate provision of transportation, water, sewerage, schools,
parks and such other public requirements.
(Prior Code, § 17.04.020) (Ord. 390, passed - -1993)
§ 156.003 JURISDICTIONAL AREA.
   The zoning jurisdiction of the city shall include the land within the
corporate limits of the city.
(Prior Code, § 17.04.030) (Ord. 390, passed - -1993)
§ 156.004 AGRICULTURE AND MINING PRODUCTION NOT AFFECTED.
   Nothing in this chapter shall be construed to prevent the use, development
or recovery of any agricultural, mineral or forest resource or product.
(Prior Code, § 17.04.040) (Ord. 390, passed - -1993)
§ 156.005 DEFINITIONS.
   (A)   (1)   Words used in the present tense include the future tense.
      (2)   Words used in the singular number include the plural; words used in
the plural include the singular, unless the natural construction of the wording
indicates otherwise.
      (3)   The word “person” includes a firm, association, corporation, trust,
organization, partnership or company, as well as an individual.
      (4)   The word “lot” includes the words “parcel” or “tract”.
      (5)   The word “shall” is mandatory; the word “may” is permissive.
(Prior Code, § 17.08.005)
   (B)   For the purpose of this chapter, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
      ACCESSORY STRUCTURE OR USE. The use or structure on the same lot with,
and customarily secondary or subordinate to, the principal use or structure.
(Prior Code, § 17.08.010)
      AUTOMOBILE WRECKING. The dismantling or wrecking of used motor vehicles
or trailers, or the storage, sale or dumping or dismantling, of partially
dismantled, obsolete or wrecked vehicles or their parts.
(Prior Code, § 17.08.015)
      BOARDING HOUSE. A building, or portion thereof, where lodging and/or
meals for five or more persons are provided for compensation.
(Prior Code, § 17.08.020)
      BUILDING. Any structure erected for support, shelter or enclosure of
persons, animals or property of any kind.
(Prior Code, § 17.08.025)
      BUILDING HEIGHT. The vertical distance from the average elevation of the
finished grade at the front of the building to the highest point of a flat
roof, the deck line of a mansard roof, or the mean height between eaves and
ridge for gable, hip and gambrel roofs.
(Prior Code, § 17.08.030)
      CARETAKER’S RESIDENCE. A single-family dwelling located in conjunction
with a land use that requires 24-hour care in order to protect or operate a
commercial or industrial firm.
(Prior Code, § 17.08.035)
      CHURCH. A building designed and used for public worship by any religious
body.
(Prior Code, § 17.08.040)
      CONDITIONAL USE. Uses, other than permitted uses, that may be allowed in
a specific district, but necessitating additional requirements to maintain and
assure the health and safety of the community and to maintain the character of
the district.
(Prior Code, § 17.08.045)
      DRIVE-IN EATING ESTABLISHMENT. A building or structure from which persons
are served food, refreshments or beverages in their vehicles or at curbside,
including establishments which may or may not serve customers outside of their
vehicles.
(Prior Code, § 17.08.050)
      DWELLING. A building or portion thereof used for occupancy by one or more
families.
(Prior Code, § 17.08.055)
      DWELLING, MOBILE HOME. A detached residential dwelling unit with minimal
dimensions of ten feet by 40 feet, fabricated at a factory and designed for
transportation on its own chassis to a building site for occupation as a
dwelling with or without a permanent foundation.
(Prior Code, § 17.08.060)
      DWELLING, MODULAR UNIT. A factory-constructed transportable building
which:
         (a)   Is designed with a permanent frame or undercarriage and to be
transported to a building site on a flatbed or trailer;
         (b)   Is designed as a detached single-family dwelling to be placed on
a permanent foundation at least 24 feet wide;
         (c)   Complies with the Montana Building, Plumbing, Electrical and
Mechanical Construction Codes and the rules for modular housing of the Building
Code Division of the Montana Department of Administration;
         (d)   Is eligible for long-term mortgage financing of at least 15
years; and
         (e)   Has siding and roofing of a type customarily used on site-
constructed residences.
(Prior Code, § 17.08.065)
      DWELLING, MULTIPLE-FAMILY. A building or portion thereof designed for
residential occupancy by four or more families living separately.
(Prior Code, § 17.08.070)
      DWELLING, SINGLE-FAMILY. A building designed for residential occupancy by
one family.
(Prior Code, § 17.08.075)
      DWELLING, TWO- OR THREE-FAMILY. A building designed for residential
occupancy by two or three families living separately.
(Prior Code, § 17.08.080)
      DWELLING UNIT. A building or portion thereof providing separate cooking,
eating, sleeping and living facilities for one family.
(Prior Code, § 17.08.085)
      FAMILY. One or more persons living together as a single housekeeping unit
and occupying a dwelling unit; provided that, unless all members are related by
blood or marriage, the FAMILY shall not exceed five persons. Domestic resident
employees serving on the premises may be counted as part of a FAMILY.
(Prior Code, § 17.08.090)
      HOME OCCUPATION. The use of a portion of a dwelling unit or accessory
building for occupations at home by one or more persons residing in the
dwelling unit. The activity must be clearly incidental and subordinate to the
use of the building as a dwelling.
(Prior Code, § 17.08.095)
      HOTEL/MOTEL. A building, or buildings, containing six or more rooms
designed and rented for sleeping purposes for transients, and where only a
general kitchen and dining room may be provided within the building or in an
accessory building.
(Prior Code, § 17.08.100)
      LOADING SPACE, OFF-STREET. An off-street space conveniently located at a
building to allow service pickups and deliveries by commercial vehicles.
(Prior Code, § 17.08.105)
      LOT. A parcel or tract of land shown as an individual unit of ownership
on a certificate of survey, subdivision plat, deed or other instrument of
record.
(Prior Code, § 17.08.110)
      LOT, CORNER. A lot located at the intersection of two or more streets.
(Prior Code, § 17.08.115)
      LOT DEPTH. The mean distance between the front and rear lot lines.
(Prior Code, § 17.08.120)
      LOT FRONTAGE. The front of a lot shall be that portion nearest the
street. For corner lots, the front of a lot shall be the narrowest part of the
lot having street frontage.
(Prior Code, § 17.08.125)
      LOT, INTERIOR. Any lot with only one frontage on a street.
(Prior Code, § 17.08.130)
      LOT LINES. The lines bounding a “lot”, as defined herein.
(Prior Code, § 17.08.135)
      LOT WIDTH. The mean width of the lot measured at right angles to its
depth, as measured at the building setback line.
(Prior Code, § 17.08.140)
      MOBILE HOME PARK. A tract of land providing for two or more mobile spaces
for lease or rent to the general public.
(Prior Code, § 17.08.145)
      NURSING HOME. A building used for the housing of and caring for
ambulatory, aged or infirmed persons by a professional staff.
(Prior Code, § 17.08.150)
      OFFICE - PROFESSIONAL, BUSINESS, ADMINISTRATIVE. Offices occupied by
accountants, architects, dentists, doctors, engineers, attorneys, insurance
agents, real estate agents or other professions.
(Prior Code, § 17.08.155)
      PARKING SPACE, OFF-STREET. A space located off any public right-of-way
which is available for parking a motor vehicle.
(Prior Code, § 17.08.160)
      RECREATION VEHICLE PARK. A premises used for public camping where persons
can rent space to park individual camping trailers, pick-up campers, motor
homes, travel trailers or automobiles for transient dwelling purposes.
(Prior Code, § 17.08.165)
      RESTAURANT. A public eating facility which does not provide curbside or
drive-in automobile service.
(Prior Code, § 17.08.170)
      RETAIL SALES. An establishment selling goods, wares or merchandise
directly to a consumer.
(Prior Code, § 17.08.175)
      SETBACK. The horizontal distance required between any structure and a lot
line, measured at right angles to the lot line.
(Prior Code, § 17.08.180)
      SHOPPING CENTER. One or more buildings containing at least three separate
retail businesses, planned, developed and managed as a unit, with off-street
parking provided on the property.
(Prior Code, § 17.08.185)
      SIGN. Any lettered or pictorial device or structure designed to inform or
attract attention.
(Prior Code, § 17.08.190)
      STRUCTURE. That which is constructed or erected at a fixed location on
the ground, or attached to something having a fixed location on the ground.
STRUCTURES include buildings, mobile homes, walls, fences and billboards or
signs.
(Prior Code, § 17.08.195)
      USE. Any purpose for which a building or other structure or a tract of
land may be designed, arranged, intended, maintained or occupied in any legal
activity, occupation, business or operation carried on or intended to be
carried on in a building or other structure or on a tract of land.
(Prior Code, § 17.08.200)
      VARIANCE. The relaxation of the strict application of the terms of this
chapter with respect to physical requirements such as yard requirements, area
requirements, building height, parking and loading requirements, where
particular conditions unique to the site of the lot would create an
unreasonable burden by making its development for permitted uses difficult or
impossible.
(Prior Code, § 17.08.205)
      WHOLESALE. The sale of goods and merchandise for resale rather than for
indirect consumption.
(Prior Code, § 17.08.210)
      YARD, FRONT. A required open space unoccupied by any structure or portion
of a structure and extending across the full width of the lot between the front
building line and the front lot line.
(Prior Code, § 17.08.215)
      YARD, REAR. A required open space unoccupied by any structure or portion
of a structure and extending across the full width of the lot between the rear
building line of the principal building and the rear lot line.
(Prior Code, § 17.08.220)
      YARD, SIDE. A required open space unoccupied by any structure or portion
of a structure and extending from the side building line to a side lot line
running from the front to the rear of the lot.
(Prior Code, § 17.08.225)
(Ord. 390, passed - -1993)
§ 156.006 REQUIREMENTS IN ALL DISTRICTS.
   The following requirements shall apply in all districts.
   (A)   Home occupations. A home occupation is an occupation conducted as a
secondary use in a dwelling; provided that:
      (1)   The use of the dwelling for the home occupation clearly must be
incidental and subordinate to its use for residential purposes, and not more
than 25% of the floor area of the dwelling may be used in the conduct of the
home occupation;
      (2)   There may be no change in the outside appearance of the building or
premises, or other visible evidence of the conduct of the home occupation other
than one sign, not exceeding six square feet in area, non-illuminated and
mounted flat against the wall of the principal structure;
      (3)   No traffic may be generated by a home occupation in greater volumes
than would normally be expected in a residential neighborhood, and any need for
parking generated by the conduct of the home occupation shall be met off the
street;
      (4)   No equipment or process shall be used in a home occupation which
creates noise, vibration, glare, fumes, odors or electrical interference
detectable to the normal senses off the lot; and
      (5)   No outdoor unenclosed storage of equipment or materials used in
connection with a home occupation occurs on the premises.
   (B)   Flood hazard areas. No building or structure may be erected or located
within an identified 100-year floodway, or any area identified by the City
Council as presenting a flood hazard. Any erection or location of buildings or
other structures must conform to Ch. 153 of this code of ordinances or the
county’s floodplain management regulations.
   (C)   Airport influence areas. No structure shall be constructed or located,
nor any tree allowed to grow to a height in excess of one foot in height for
each 20 feet in horizontal distance beginning at a point 200 feet from the end
of each runway and extending to a distance of 5,200 feet from the end of the
runway. The above requirement shall apply to an area having a width of 250 feet
beginning at a point 200 feet from the end of each runway, widening thereafter
uniformly to a width of 1,250 feet at a distance of 5,300 feet beyond the end
of the runway, its centerline being the continuation of the centerline of the
runway.
   (D)   Visibility at intersections. On a corner lot in any residential
district, the following criteria must be followed:
      (1)   Measuring from corner 25 feet in both directions along the curb a
triangle is formed.
      (2)   The following restrictions will apply:
         (a)   Maximum height of any new object(s) in the triangle section
shall be 12 inches from top of curb;
         (b)   Any corner with a fire hydrant shall comply with the current
Fire Code;
         (c)   No new trees shall be planted in a triangle;
         (d)   All existing trees shall be trimmed up to eight feet and shall
not be replaced; and
         (e)   All existing hedges, bushes, shrubs and other objects shall have
a maximum height of 30 inches from top of curb and shall not be replaced.
   (E)   Structure to have access. Every principal building erected or placed
on a lot shall have access to a public street or any approved private street
other than an alley, and all structures shall be so located on lots as to
provide required off-street parking and safe and convenient access for fire
protection.
   (F)   Exceptions to height regulations. The height limitations contained in
the district regulations do not apply to spires, belfries, cupolas, antennas,
water tanks, ventilators, chimneys or other appurtenances not intended for
human occupancy and usually required to be placed above the roof level.
(Prior Code, § 17.52.010) (Ord. 390, passed - -1993; Ord. 432, passed - -2007)

fees and charges and a collection procedure for building permits, zoning
permits, conditional use permits, variances and appeals.
   (B)   Payment required. Until all applicable fees and charges have been paid
in full, no action may be taken on any application or appeal.

ADMINISTRATION
§ 156.020 ZONING ADMINISTRATOR.
   (A)   Designation of Zoning Administrator. A Zoning Administrator designated
by the City Council shall administer and enforce this chapter. The
Administrator may be provided with assistance of city personnel or departments
as the City Council may direct.
   (B)   Duties of the Zoning Administrator.
      (1)   The Zoning Administrator shall receive applications for zoning
permits and conditional use permits, review applications and plans, issue
zoning permits and coordinate inspection of premises and properties.
      (2)   Where the Zoning Administrator finds that any of the provisions of
this chapter are being violated, he or she shall notify in writing the person
responsible for such violations, indicating the nature of the violation and
ordering the action necessary to correct it. He or she shall order
discontinuance of illegal buildings or structural changes; or shall take any
other action authorized by this chapter to ensure compliance with or to prevent
violation of its provisions.
(Prior Code, § 17.12.010) (Ord. 390, passed - -1993)
§ 156.021 ZONING COMMISSION.
   (A)   The City Council shall establish a Zoning Commission and appoint
members to the Commission.
   (B)   The Zoning Commission shall have the following duties:
      (1)   Review and recommend proposals for the amendment of this chapter
and the official zoning map; and
      (2)   Review and approve applications for conditional use permits under
the procedures set forth in §§
156.235 through
156.237 of this chapter.
(Prior Code, § 17.12.020) (Ord. 390, passed - -1993)
§ 156.022 BOARD OF ADJUSTMENT.
   (A)   Board of Adjustment established. A Board of Adjustment (hereinafter
referred to as “the Board”) is hereby established in accordance with M.C.A. §§
76-2-321 through 76-2-328. The Board shall be comprised of five members
appointed by the City Council, each for a term of three years, except that in
the initial appointment, one member shall be appointed for a term of one year,
two members for a term of two years and two members for a term of three years.
Members of the Board may be removed from office by the City Council for cause
upon written charges and after public hearing. Vacancies on the Board shall be
filled by resolution of the City Council for the unexpired term of the member
affected.
   (B)   Proceedings of the Board of Adjustment.
      (1)   The Board shall select one of its members as Chairperson and shall
adopt rules necessary to conduct its affairs in keeping with the provisions of
this chapter. Meetings shall be held at the call of the Chairperson and at such
other times as the Board may determine. The Chairperson or, in his or her
absence, the acting Chairperson may administer oaths and compel the attendance
of witnesses. Meetings shall be open to the public.
      (2)   The Board shall keep minutes of its proceedings, showing the vote
of each member upon question, or if absent or failing to vote indicating such
fact, and shall keep records of its examinations and other official actions,
all of which shall be a public record and be immediately filed in the office of
the Board.
   (C)   Powers of the Board of Adjustment. The Board shall have the following
powers:
      (1)   To authorize, upon application in specific cases, such variance
from the requirements of this chapter specified below as will not be contrary
to the public interest, where owing to special physical configurations of a
property, a literal enforcement of the provisions of this chapter will result
in unnecessary hardship, and that the spirit of this chapter shall be observed.
More specifically, the Board may, after public notice and hearing,
conditionally approve, deny or approve any request to modify the following
requirements of this chapter:
         (a)   Setback requirements;
         (b)   Yard requirements;
         (c)   Area requirements;
         (d)   Height and width requirements;
         (e)   Parking requirements; and
         (f)   Loading requirements.
      (2)   Neither the non-conforming use of neighboring lands, structures or
buildings in the same district, nor the permitted or non-conforming use of
lands, structures or buildings in other districts are grounds for the issuance
of a variance; and
      (3)   To grant a variance the Board must make a finding that the granting
of the variance will be in harmony with the general purpose and intent of this
chapter, will not be injurious to the neighborhood, is the minimum variance
that will make possible the reasonable use of the land, building or structure,
or otherwise be detrimental to the public welfare. In addition, the Board must
determine:
         (a)   That special conditions and circumstances exist which are
peculiar to the land, structure or building involved and which are not
applicable to other lands, structures or buildings in the same district;
         (b)   That literal interpretation of the provisions of this chapter
would deprive the applicant of rights commonly enjoyed by other properties in
the same district under the terms of this chapter;
         (c)   That the special conditions and circumstances do not result from
the action of the applicant; and
         (d)   That granting the requested variance will not confer on the
applicant any special privilege that is denied by this chapter to other lands,
structures or buildings in the same district.
   (D)   Procedure of Board of Adjustment.
      (1)   Applications for a variance may be submitted to the Board of
Adjustment by any person as provided by the rules of the Board, by filing with
the Zoning Administrator an application for variance.
      (2)   The application for appeal must specifically set forth the grounds
of the variance, as indicated on the application form.
      (3)   The Board shall fix a reasonable time for the hearing of appeal,
shall give notice of the hearing at least seven days prior to the holding of a
public hearing and shall notify by mail the property owner requesting the
variance.
      (4)   At the hearing, any party may appear in person, or by agent or
attorney.
(Prior Code, § 17.12.030) (Ord. 390, passed - -1993)
§ 156.023 APPEALS.
   (A)   Appeal to City Council.
      (1)   The City Council shall hear and decide appeals where it is alleged
there is error in any order, requirement, decision or determination made by an
administrative official in the enforcement of this chapter.
      (2)   In exercising this power, the City Council may, in conformity with
the provisions of this chapter, reverse or affirm, wholly or in part, or modify
the order, decision or determination appealed and may make such order, decision
or determination as deemed necessary and, to that end, shall have powers of the
administrative official whose decision is appealed.
   (B)   Variances or appeals may not allow uses not permitted.
      (1)   Under no circumstances may the Board of Adjustment grant a
variance, nor the City Council grant an appeal, that would allow a use not
permissible under the terms of this chapter in the district involved, or any
use expressly or by implication prohibited by the terms of this chapter in the
district.
      (2)   The City Council may, at its discretion, modify or waive the
requirements of §
156.209 of this chapter.
   (C)   Stay of proceedings. An appeal stays all proceedings in furtherance of
the action appealed, unless the administrative official from whom the appeal is
taken, certifies to the Board of Adjustment after the notice of appeal is
filed, that by reason of facts stated in the certificate, a stay would, in his
or her opinion, cause imminent peril to life or property. In such case,
proceedings shall not be stayed other than by a restraining order which may be
ordered by the Board or by a court of record on application, on notice to the
officer from whom the appeal is taken and on due cause shown.
   (D)   Appeals from decisions of the Board of Adjustment or City Council.
      (1)   Any person or persons, jointly or severally, aggrieved by any
decision of the Board of Adjustment or City Council, or any taxpayer, may
present to a court of record a petition, duly verified, setting forth that such
decision is illegal, in whole or in part, specifying the grounds of the
illegality. Such petition shall be presented to the court within 30 days after
the filing of the decision of the Board of Adjustment or City Council.
      (2)   Upon presentation of such petition, the court may allow a writ of
certiorari directed to the Board or Council to review such decision of the
Board or Council and shall prescribe therein the time within which a return
thereto must be made and served upon the relator’s attorney, which may not be
less than ten days and may be extended by the court. The allowance of the writ
shall not stay proceedings upon the decision appealed from, but the court may,
on application, on notice to the Board and on due cause shown, grant a
restraining order.
      (3)   The Board or Council need not return the original papers acted upon
by it, but may return certified or sworn copies thereof or of such portions
thereof as may be called for by such writ. The return shall concisely set forth
such other facts as may be pertinent and material to show the grounds of the
decision appealed from and shall be verified.
      (4)   If, upon hearing, it appears to the court that testimony is
necessary for the proper disposition of the matter, it may take evidence or
appoint a referee to take such evidence as it may direct and report the same to
the court with his or her findings of fact and conclusions of law, which
constitutes a part of the proceedings upon which the determination of the court
will be made. The court may reverse or affirm, wholly or partly, or may modify
the decision brought up for review.
      (5)   Costs shall not be allowed against the Board or Council unless it
appears to the court that it acted with gross negligence, or in bad faith, or
with malice in making the decision appealed from.
(Prior Code, § 17.12.040) (Ord. 390, passed - -1993)
PERMITS; DISTRICTS REQUIREMENTS; OFFICIAL ZONING MAP
§ 156.035 PERMIT REQUIRED.
   (A)   (1)   A zoning permit must be obtained from the city’s Zoning
Administrator before any building, other structure or land may be used or
occupied, or before any building or other structure permitted under this
chapter may be erected, moved, expanded or structurally altered.
      (2)   The Zoning Administrator may issue a zoning permit only when the
proposed building, structure, parcel or use will meet the requirements of this
chapter.
   (B)   The requirements of this chapter operate in addition to those
requirements established under other city code provisions; except that, where
conflicts with other city code provisions may occur, these zoning requirements
shall govern.
   (C)   A conditional use permit must be obtained from the Zoning Commission
before those uses specified as conditional uses within certain zoning districts
may be established. The Zoning Commission may issue a conditional use permit
only when the proposed use will meet both the requirements of the particular
district involved and the conditions specified for the use.
   (D)   Any person required to obtain a zoning permit or conditional use
permit under these regulations must submit to the Zoning Administrator an
application with all the required information specified by the application.
(Prior Code, § 17.16.010) (Ord. 390, passed - -1993)
§ 156.036 DISTRICTS ESTABLISHED.
   Within the jurisdictional area specified in §
156.003 of this chapter, zoning districts are hereby established and are shown
on the official zoning map described in §
156.038 of this chapter. Sections
156.055 through
156.063,
156.075 through
156.085,

156.205 through

by any proposed building, structure or use located within each district.
(Prior Code, § 17.16.020) (Ord. 390, passed - -1993)
§ 156.037 INTERPRETATION OF DISTRICT BOUNDARIES.
   Where uncertainty may exist as to the location of district boundaries as
shown on the official zoning map, the following rules shall apply in
interpreting the nearest logical line to that shown.
   (A)   Boundaries shall be construed as following center lines of streets,
highways or alleys.
   (B)   Boundaries shall be construed as following the center lines of
streams, rivers, canals or ditches.
   (C)   Boundaries shall be construed as following a line midway between the
main tracks of a railroad right-of-way.
   (D)   Boundaries shall be construed as following platted lot lines.
   (E)   Boundaries shall be construed as following the boundaries of the
incorporated city limits.
   (F)   Boundaries shall be construed as parallel to or extensions of features
indicated on the official zoning map.
   (G)   Where physical or cultural features existing on the ground are
different from those shown on the official zoning map, or where circumstances
arise not covered by the rules above, the Board of Adjustment shall interpret
the district boundaries.
(Prior Code, § 17.16.030) (Ord. 390, passed - -1993)
§ 156.038 INCORPORATION OF OFFICIAL ZONING MAP.
   (A)   The “Official Zoning Map of Malta, Montana” and all notations,
references and other information on the map are hereby incorporated by
reference and made a part of this chapter.
   (B)   The official zoning map shall be kept in City Hall and shall be the
final authority as to the current status of zoning districts in the city’s
zoning jurisdictional area.
   (C)   The official zoning map shall bear the signature of the Mayor,
attested by the City Clerk, and the date of adoption of the ordinance.
   (D)   The official zoning map shall bear the seal of the city under the
following words, “This is to certify that this is the Official Zoning Map of
Malta referred to in Section 9 of Ordinance Number 390 of the City of Malta”.
(Prior Code, § 17.16.040) (Ord. 390, passed - -1993)
§ 156.039 AMENDMENTS.
   (A)   Whenever any changes are made to district boundaries in accordance
with the procedures of this chapter, those changes approved by the City Council
promptly shall be entered on the official zoning map, and a signed and dated
certification attached to the map. No amendment to district boundaries shall
become effective until those changes are presented to the City Council by the
Zoning Administrator. If the City Council approves the changes, the changes
shall be entered on the official zoning map.
   (B)   No changes of any nature shall be made to the official zoning map,
except in conformity with the procedures specified in this chapter.
   (C)   (1)   A copy of the official zoning map, duly certified by the Zoning
Administrator shall be filed in the office of the Clerk and Recorder of the
county.
      (2)   Each change to the official zoning map adopted by the City Council,
duly certified by the Zoning Administrator, shall likewise be filed in the
office of the Clerk and Recorder.
      (3)   Any changes adopted by the City Council to the official zoning map
must be approved by resolution of the City Council and approved by the Mayor.
(Prior Code, § 17.16.050) (Ord. 390, passed - -1993)
§ 156.040 ADOPTION OF NEW MAP.
   (A)   In the event that the official zoning map becomes damaged, destroyed,
lost or difficult to interpret, the City Council may, by resolution, adopt a
new official zoning map.
   (B)   The new official zoning map may correct drafting or other errors or
omissions in the prior map, but no such corrections shall have the effect of
amending the original official zoning map or any subsequent amendment thereof.
   (B)   The new map shall be certified in the same manner as the original
official zoning map, noting that it supersedes the prior map.
(Prior Code, § 17.16.060) (Ord. 390, passed - -1993)
LOW DENSITY RESIDENTIAL DISTRICT (R-1)
§ 156.055 PURPOSE.
   This district is intended provide for the development of single-family
residences and two- or three-family residences at a density compatible with
existing residential development. This district also accommodates those
institutional and public uses compatible with residential neighborhoods.
(Prior Code, § 17.20.010) (Ord. 390, passed - -1993)
§ 156.056 PERMITTED PRINCIPAL USES.
   The following uses are permitted within this district; provided that, only
one principal use or structure is allowed on a single lot:
   (A)   A church or other place of worship;
   (B)   A nursing home;
   (C)   A park or playground;
   (D)   A public or private school;
   (E)   A single-family dwelling constructed on-site, or assembled as a
modular unit which meets the definition in §
156.005 of this chapter; a mobile home or mobile home court is not permitted;
and
   (F)   A two- or three-family dwelling, constructed on-site and containing
only one story.
(Prior Code, § 17.20.020) (Ord. 390, passed - -1993)

   The following accessory and temporary uses are permitted in this district:
   (A)   Accessory buildings and uses incidental to the above principal uses;

§ 156.059 LOT AREA AND WIDTH.
   Except for existing lots of record which, because of ownership, cannot be
reassembled to conform to this requirement, the following lot areas and widths
are required.
   (A)   Single-family dwelling. Each lot shall contain a minimum of 7,000
square feet, and be at least 50 feet wide.
   (B)   Two- and three-family dwellings. Each lot shall contain a minimum of
4,000 square feet per dwelling unit, and be at least 50 feet wide.
(Prior Code, § 17.20.050) (Ord. 390, passed - -1993)
§ 156.060 YARD REQUIREMENTS.
   Every lot shall have the following yard requirements as measured from the
farthest extension of the structure.
   (A)   Front yard.
      (1)   A 30-foot yard shall be provided on all street frontages (as
measured from curbline, drainage swale or equivalent drainage facility).
      (2)   Corner lots shall be construed as having two frontages, each of
which shall allow for a 30-foot yard.
   (B)   Side yard. Side yards abutting interior lot lines shall not be less
than three feet.
   (C)   Rear yard. A rear yard of at least three feet shall be provided.
   (D)   Determination. In determining building lines and yard requirements,
the farthermost protruding part of a structure shall be the determining factor.
(Prior Code, § 17.20.060) (Ord. 390, passed - -1993)
§ 156.061 BUILDING HEIGHT.
   (A)   Maximum height for all buildings and other structures shall be 24
feet.
   (B)   Maximum height for accessory buildings may not exceed one and one-half
times the height of the primary dwelling, and shall not exceed 24 feet for
single-family dwellings and two- or three-family dwellings containing only one
story.
   (C)   (1)   Accessory buildings located on the same lot (not involving the
conduct of a business) including two private garages, or community garage.
      (2)   Garages shall not exceed the following sizes for each lot:
 
Lot Size                                Maximum Garage Size
3,900 square feet to 7,000 square feet  1,000 square feet
7,001 square feet to 10,000 square feet 1,200 square feet
Over 10,000 square feet                 1,600 square feet
 
      (3)   Accessory buildings must comply with all setback requirements.
   (D)   No former railcars, semi boxes, containers or corn-parables will be
allowed for storage units.
   (E)   Garages must be new, permanent structures and shall have a dwelling
located on lot(s).
   (F)   A maximum of two garages will be allowed, whether attached or
detached.
(Prior Code, § 17.20.070) (Ord. 390, passed - -1993; Ord. 413, passed - -2003;
Ord. 434, passed - -2010; Ord. 438, passed - -2011)
§ 156.062 SIGNS.
   The following signs are permitted in this district:
   (A)   For residential uses, non-illuminated signs less than six square feet
in area; and
   (B)   For all other uses, non-illuminated signs, including bulletin boards
at schools and churches, not exceeding 12 square feet in area; provided, the
sign is located at least ten feet from any road right-of- way and does not
obstruct traffic visibility.
(Prior Code, § 17.20.080) (Ord. 390, passed - -1993)
§ 156.063 GARAGES ON VACANT LOTS.
   One garage shall be allowed on a vacant lot with the following criteria:
   (A)   Section 156.061(C) of this chapter for garage size allowed shall be
followed;
   (B)   Maximum height is not to exceed 24 feet;
   (C)   Residential use only, no commercial use allowed;
   (D)   Garage must be placed on a cement foundation that meets the city’s
Building Codes, and placed toward the rear of a vacant lot to accommodate for a
home to be built at a later date;
   (E)   Proposed garage must have four walls, roof and siding that meet
Current Building Codes and an operational door. Pole barns are not an option in
this area; and
   (F)   Only one building per lot without a house will be allowed, either a
garage or storage shed.
(Prior Code, § 17.20.010) (Ord. 434, passed - -2010)
MEDIUM DENSITY RESIDENTIAL DISTRICT (R-2)
§ 156.075 PURPOSE.
   (A)   The purpose of this district is to recognize the existing residential
neighborhoods of the city, as well as those areas which are deemed appropriate
for residential expansions. A variety of residential types and densities,
including multiple-family, will be accommodated to provide a balance within the
community.
   (B)   It is intended that this district be maintained and expanded to
preserve the residential attractiveness in a mixed use atmosphere.
   (C)   This district also will accommodate those institutional and public
uses compatible with residential neighborhoods.
(Prior Code, § 17.24.010) (Ord. 390, passed - -1993)
§ 156.076 PERMITTED PRINCIPAL USES.
   The following uses are permitted within this district; provided that, only
one principal use or structure is allowed on a single lot:
   (A)   Boarding house;

   (C)   Funeral home/mortuary without crematorium;
   (D)   Hospital;
   (E)   Library; museum;
   (F)   Multiple-family dwelling;
   (G)   Nursing home;
   (H)   One-story professional office building;
   (I)   Park or recreation facility;
   (J)   Public or private school;
   (K)   Single-family residence; and
   (L)   Two- or three-family dwelling.
(Prior Code, § 17.24.020) (Ord. 390, passed - -1993; Ord. 397, passed - -2000)

           accommodate the mobile homes anticipated
           The mobile home concrete ribbon footings must be improved to support the
           mobile home and be provided with 4 anchors or tie-downs to assure the
           stability of the home
           At least a 20-foot separation is required between mobile homes,
           including their attached structures, such as awnings or carports
           No detached structure, such as a storage shed, may be located within 5
           feet of any mobile home or its attached structures

(Prior Code, § 17.24.030) (Ord. 390, passed - -1993; Ord. 396, passed - -1995)
§ 156.078 ACCESSORY AND TEMPORARY USES.
   The following accessory and temporary uses are permitted in this district:
   (A)   Accessory buildings and uses incidental to the above uses;
   (B)   Driveways, sidewalks, patios, retaining walls and steps require a
permit. No fee charge;

   (D)   Temporary buildings for and during construction only.
(Prior Code, § 17.24.040) (Ord. 390, passed - -1993)
§ 156.079 SPECIAL PROVISIONS; MOBILE HOMES.
   (A)   Mobile homes in place at the passage time of this section will be
allowed to remain and to be replaced.
   (B)   All replacement mobile homes in R-2 Districts will comply with §
156.104 of this chapter.
(Prior Code, § 17.24.050) (Ord. 390, passed - -1993)
§ 156.080 YARD REQUIREMENTS.
   Every lot shall have the following yard requirements as measured from the
farthest extension of the structure.
   (A)   Front yard. A 30-foot yard shall be provided on all street frontages
(as measured from the curb, drainage or equivalent drainage facility). Corner
lots shall be construed as having two frontages, each of which shall allow a
30-foot yard with the exception of corner lots located on streets with 60-foot
rights- of-way, which shall allow for a 20-foot yard. Exception: or a yard that
matches the established building line on that block.
   (B)   Side yard. Side yards abutting interior lot lines shall not be less
than three feet.
   (C)   Rear yard. Rear yards of at least 15 feet shall be provided; except
where a garage is located within the rear yard, the rear yard may be reduced to
three feet.
   (D)   Determination. In determining building and yard requirements, the
eaves shall be the determining factor.
   (E)   Entrance landing. A five-foot open entrance landing shall be allowed
to all structures; provided, it remains three feet back from interior property
line.
(Prior Code, § 17.24.060) (Ord. 390, passed - -1993; Ord. 413, passed - -2003)
§ 156.081 LOT AREA AND WIDTH.
   Except for existing lots of record which, because of ownership, cannot be
reassembled to conform to this requirement, the following lot areas and widths
are required.
   (A)   Single-family dwelling. Each lot shall contain a minimum of 7,000
square feet, and be at least 50 feet wide.
   (B)   Two- or three-family dwellings. Each lot shall contain a minimum of
4,000 square feet per dwelling unit, and be at least 50 feet wide.
(Prior Code, § 17.24.070) (Ord. 390, passed - -1993)
§ 156.082 BUILDING HEIGHT.
   (A)   Maximum building height shall be 24 feet for single-family dwellings
and all listed permitted principal uses and 32 feet for multiple-family
dwellings consisting of more than two units.
   (B)   Maximum height for accessory buildings may not exceed one and one-half
times the height of the primary dwelling, and shall not exceed 24 feet for
single-family or 32 feet for multiple-family dwellings consisting of more than
two units.
   (C)   (1)   Accessory buildings located on the same lot (not involving the
conduct of a business), including two private garages, or community garage.
Garages shall not exceed the following sizes for each lot:
 
Lot Size                    Maximum Garage Size
3,900 to 7,000 square feet  1,000 square feet
7,001 to 10,000 square feet 1,200 square feet
Over 10,000 square feet     1,600 square feet
 
      (2)   Accessory buildings must comply with all setback requirements.
   (D)   No former railcars, semi boxes, containers or comparables will be
allowed for storage units.
   (E)   Garages must be new, permanent structures and shall have a dwelling
located on lot(s).
   (F)   A maximum of two garages will be allowed, whether attached or
detached.
(Prior Code, § 17.24.080) (Ord. 390, passed - -1993; Ord. 413, passed - -2003;
Ord. 434, passed - -2010; Ord. 438, passed - -2011)
§ 156.083 OFF-STREET PARKING.
   (A)   Single-family dwellings. Two off-street parking spaces are required
per dwelling unit.
   (B)   Multiple-family dwellings. One and one-half off-street parking spaces
are required per dwelling unit.
   (C)   Compliance. Numbers of non-residential parking spaces and all off-
street parking requirements shall comply with §
156.220 of this chapter.
(Prior Code, § 17.24.090) (Ord. 390, passed - -1993)
§ 156.084 SIGNS.
   (A)   For residential uses, non-illuminated signs of less than six square
feet in area; and
   (B)   For all other uses, non-illuminated signs, including bulletin boards
at schools and churches, not exceeding 12 square feet in area; provided, the
sign is located at least ten feet from any street right-of- way and does not
obstruct traffic visibility.
(Prior Code, § 17.24.100) (Ord. 390, passed - -1993)
§ 156.085 GARAGES ON VACANT LOTS.
   One garage shall be allowed on a vacant lot with the following criteria:
   (A)   Section
156.082(C) of this chapter for garage size allowed shall be followed;
   (B)   Maximum height is not to exceed 24 feet;
   (C)   Residential use only, no commercial use is allowed;
   (D)   Garage must be placed on a cement foundation that meets the city’s
Building Codes, and placed toward the rear of a vacant lot to accommodate for a
home to be built at a later date;
   (E)   Proposed garage must have four walls, roof and siding that meet
current Building Codes and an operational door. Pole barns are not an option in
this area; and
   (F)   Only one building per lot without a house will be allowed, either a
garage or a storage shed.
(Prior Code, § 17.24.110) (Ord. 434, passed - -2010)
MOBILE HOME SUBDIVISIONS (R-3)
§ 156.100 PURPOSE.
   (A)   The purpose of this district is to recognize the existing residential
neighborhoods of the city, as well as those areas which are deemed appropriate
for mobile home subdivisions.
   (B)   A variety of residential types and densities, including two- or three-
family dwellings and mobile homes, will be accommodated to provide a balance
within the community.
   (C)   It is intended that this district be maintained and expanded to
preserve the residential attractiveness in a mixed use atmosphere.
(Prior Code, § 17.28.010) (Ord. 390, passed - -1993)
§ 156.101 PERMITTED PRINCIPAL USES.
   The following uses are permitted within this district; provided that, only
one principal use or structure is allowed on a single lot:
   (A)   A church or any other place of worship;
   (B)   A mobile home, under special provisions;
   (C)   A park or recreation facility;
   (D)   A single-family residence; and
   (E)   A two- or three-family residence.
(Prior Code, § 17.28.020) (Ord. 390, passed - -1993)
§ 156.102 CONDITIONAL USES.
   None.
(Prior Code, § 17.28.030) (Ord. 390, passed - -1993)
§ 156.103 ACCESSORY AND TEMPORARY USES.
   The following accessory and temporary uses are permitted in this district:
   (A)   Accessory buildings and uses incidental to the above uses;
   (B)   Driveways, sidewalks, patios, retaining walls and steps require a
permit. No fee charge;
   (C)   Home occupations under the requirements of §
156.006 of this chapter; and
   (D)   Temporary buildings for and during construction only.
(Prior Code, § 17.28.040) (Ord. 390, passed - -1993)
§ 156.104 SPECIAL PROVISIONS; MOBILE HOMES.
   (A)   (1)   Each mobile home lot must be provided with concrete ribbon
footings that must be improved to support the mobile home and be provided with
at least four anchors or cable tie downs for securing the mobile home.
      (2)   The Building Inspector must approve.
   (B)   Each mobile home must be properly skirted, entirely enclosing the
bottom section within 60 days after placement.
   (C)   Each mobile home must be provided with adequate storage space, such as
access in skirting or an accessory building.
   (D)   Only one mobile home may be located on a single lot.
   (E)   Each mobile home shall have a minimum of 900 square feet of floor
space.
   (F)   Each mobile home shall have utilities connected in accordance with the
city and state requirements. All mobile homes must be connected to city water
and sewer.
   (G)   Each mobile home may not be over 20 years of age from time of approval
to place within the city limits.
   (H)   Each mobile home shall have siding, skirting and roofing materials of
a type customarily used on site-constructed residences (examples: steel; wood;
vinyl siding).
(Prior Code, § 17.28.050) (Ord. 390, passed - -1993; Ord. 433, passed - -2009)
§ 156.105 YARD REQUIREMENTS.
   Every lot shall have the following yard requirements as measured from the
farthest extension of the structure.
   (A)   Front yard.
      (1)   A 30-foot yard shall be provided on all street frontages (as
measured from the curb, drainage or equivalent drainage facility).
      (2)   Corner lots shall be construed as having two frontages, each of
which shall allow a 30-foot yard with the exception of corner lots located on
streets with 60-foot rights-of-way, which shall allow for a 20-foot yard.
      (3)   Exception: none.
   (B)   Side yard. Side yards abutting interior lot lines shall not be less
than three feet.
   (C)   Rear yard. Rear yards of at least three feet shall be provided.
   (D)   Determination. In determining building and yard requirements, the
eaves shall be the determining factor.
   (E)   Entrance landing. A five-foot open entrance landing shall be allowed
to all structures; provided, it remains three feet back from the interior
property line.

CENTRAL BUSINESS DISTRICT (CBD)
§ 156.125 PURPOSE.
   The Central Business District is intended to be the central focus of the
city’s business, government, service and cultural activities. The uses in this
district should be those which are appropriate in a high density, intensively
developed commercial center. Appropriate area should be provided for the
logical and planned expansion of the present district. The area should be
developed as an attractive, functional and convenient commercial environment,
and to provide the mix of activities necessary to maintain a downtown
character.
(Prior Code, § 17.32.010) (Ord. 390, passed - -1993)
§ 156.126 PERMITTED PRINCIPAL USES.
   The following uses are permitted within this district:
   (A)   Amusement centers, recreational facilities located in enclosed
buildings;
   (B)   Apartments, located above the first floor;
   (C)   Auditoriums, theaters;
   (D)   Building materials and equipment sales;
   (E)   Clubs and lodges;
   (F)   Financial institutions;
   (G)   Funeral homes;
   (H)   Government, educational and institutional uses;
   (I)   Hotels, motels;
   (J)   Libraries;
   (K)   Medical and dentist offices, clinics and laboratories;
   (L)   Museums and art galleries;
   (M)   Nursing homes;
   (N)   Offices - professional, business, administrative, services;
   (O)   Parking areas;
   (P)   Police and fire stations;
   (Q)   Recreational facilities;
   (R)   Restaurants, taverns, nightclubs (but not drive-in eating
establishments);
   (S)   Retail businesses or services, whose activities primarily are
conducted within an enclosed building;
   (T)   Sales, service and repair - motor vehicles (including service
stations); agricultural implements, equipment and materials;
   (U)   Senior citizen centers; and
   (V)   Other uses commensurate with the above uses and compatible with the
purpose of this district.
(Prior Code, § 17.32.020) (Ord. 390, passed - -1993)
§ 156.127 ACCESSORY AND TEMPORARY USES.
   (A)   Accessory buildings and uses incidental to the principal uses;
   (B)   Buildings or structures used for and during construction or grading;
   (C)   Sale of Christmas trees, baked goods, clothing or like products where
no permanent structure is erected;
   (D)   Temporary signs; and
   (E)   Use of open land for meetings, circuses, carnivals.
(Prior Code, § 17.32.030) (Ord. 390, passed - -1993)
§ 156.128 LOT AREA, WIDTH AND COVERAGE; FLOOR AREA.
   No requirements are specified for lot area, lot width, lot coverage, nor for
floor area.
(Prior Code, § 17.32.040) (Ord. 390, passed - -1993)
§ 156.129 BUILDING HEIGHT.
   Maximum building height shall be 45 feet.
(Prior Code, § 17.32.050) (Ord. 390, passed - -1993)
§ 156.130 YARD REQUIREMENTS.
   (A)   Front yard. Any building or structure must be set back to legal
property line.
   (B)   Side yard. Side yards abutting interior lot lines shall not be less
than three feet unless Building Codes allow closer placement.
   (C)   Rear yard. Any building or structure must be at least ten feet from
the rear property line.
(Prior Code, § 17.32.060) (Ord. 390, passed - -1993; Ord. 429, passed - -2007)
§ 156.131 OFF-STREET PARKING AND LOADING AREAS.
   (A)   No off-street parking is required in the Central Business District.
   (B)   Off-street loading requirements of §
156.221 of this chapter must be met.
(Prior Code, § 17.32.070) (Ord. 390, passed - -1993)
HIGHWAY COMMERCIAL DISTRICT (H-C)
§ 156.145 PURPOSE.
   This district is intended to accommodate the business and light industrial
uses which require more space than is normally available in the Central
Business District, or whose operations require access to the major
transportation facilities serving the community. The district should
accommodate these uses while preserving the traffic-carrying capacity of the
road system and the desirability of abutting land for residential development.
(Prior Code, § 17.36.010) (Ord. 390, passed - -1993)
§ 156.146 PERMITTED PRINCIPAL USES.
   The following uses are permitted within this district:
   (A)   Amusement centers and recreational facilities located in enclosed
buildings;
   (B)   Automobile and truck sales, service and repair; all uses pertaining
to, including service stations and car washes;
   (C)   Beverage bottling and distributing;
   (D)   Building equipment and materials - wholesale and retail, including
storage yards;
   (E)   Cleaning and drying establishments;
   (F)   Electric equipment - assembly, repair and sales;
   (G)   Fraternal lodges and clubs;
   (H)   Laboratories;
   (I)   Meeting halls, auditoriums, arenas, indoor theaters;
   (J)   Motels, hotels, convention centers;
   (K)   Outdoor advertising;
   (L)   Police and fire stations;
   (M)   Restaurants, drive-in eating establishments, nightclubs;
   (N)   Retail and wholesale sales, service and repair - agricultural
products, products serving agriculture, farm implements, heavy machinery,
mobile homes, travel trailers, recreational vehicles;
   (O)   Storage yards;
   (P)   Utilities, public or private;
   (Q)   Veterinary office, clinic, hospital;
   (R)   Warehouses;
   (S)   Wholesale storage or sales; and
   (T)   Other uses commensurate with the above uses and compatible with the
purpose of this district.
(Prior Code, § 17.36.020) (Ord. 390, passed - -1993)

§ 156.153 SIGNS.
   Signs within this district shall comply with regulations enforced by state
and federal agencies.
(Prior Code, § 17.36.090) (Ord. 390, passed - -1993)
§ 156.154 ACCESS POINTS ONTO PUBLIC ROADS.
   (A)   Approaches onto public roads and highways shall be at least 32 feet
wide.
   (B)   Approaches onto public roads and highways shall have a grade of 6% or
less.
   (C)   (1)   Approaches onto public roads or highways shall be at least 125
feet apart.
      (2)   The centerline of approaches from properties on opposite sides of a
public road shall be aligned at the same point on the public road.
(Prior Code, § 17.36.100) (Ord. 390, passed - -1993)
§ 156.155 GRADING AND DRAINAGE.
   (A)   The site shall be graded and appropriate drainage facilities installed
to remove surface run-off waters in a manner that will not affect adjacent or
nearby properties, rivers or public roads.
   (B)   Culverts, curbs, gutters, ditches, swales and other drainage
facilities shall be installed to assure that approaches, parking areas and
other traffic facilities do not obstruct drainage facilities or adversely
affect public road and traffic facilities.
   (C)   Culverts and bridges shall be large enough to accommodate potential
runoff from upstream drainage areas.
   (D)   Curbs and gutters or swales shall be required according to the
character of the area, density of development and nature of adjoining
properties and public streets.
(Prior Code, § 17.36.110) (Ord. 390, passed - -1993)
GENERAL INDUSTRIAL DISTRICT (I)
§ 156.170 PURPOSE.
   This district is intended vide for efficient and functional operation of
heavy commercial, manufacturing, processing and other industrial uses in
appropriate locations. Industrial uses which produce noise, smoke, dirt,
vibration, glare or similarly obtrusive nuisances shall be regulated to
minimize the impact on the public health and safety. These activities generally
require reasonable access to major transportation facilities, need extensive
open storage and service areas and generate heavy traffic. To help assure
efficiency and function of industrial uses, protection from incompatible
residential and commercial uses is necessary.
(Prior Code, § 17.40.010) (Ord. 390, passed - -1993)
§ 156.171 PERMITTED USES.
   (A)   Agricultural products processing, storage, loading;
   (B)   Automobile, truck, farm machinery, heavy equipment repair;
   (C)   Cement, concrete and paving products, including mixing plants;
   (D)   Fabrication or assembly of products from prestructured materials or
compounds;
   (E)   Freight terminals truck or rail;
   (F)   Industrial laboratories;
   (G)   Manufacturing or processing:
      (1)   Products from organic material, chemicals, glass, metal, minerals,
stones or earth; and
      (2)   Foodstuffs, textiles, electrical components, wood, leather, paper
or plastic.
   (H)   Railroads, all uses associated with operations of;
   (I)   Signs - billboards;
   (J)   Storage yards;
   (K)   Utilities;
   (L)   Warehousing; and
   (M)   Welding or sheet metal shops.
(Prior Code, § 17.40.020) (Ord. 390, passed - -1993)

slaughterhouses    or a screen of evergreen shrubs or trees at least 8 feet
                   high at maturity must be planted. The fence or screen must
                   be maintained
 
(Prior Code, § 17.40.030) (Ord. 390, passed - -1993)

   (A)   Accommodations for caretakers, watchmen and custodians;

no permanent structure is erected;

and grading; and

   (A)   Where public water and sewer service is available, no minimum lot size
is required.

required, that agency shall determine the lot size.
   (C)   Where neither of the above conditions applies, the minimum lot size
shall be one acre.

feet.

   (A)   Approaches onto public roads and highways shall be at least 32 feet
wide.
   (B)   Approaches onto public roads and highways shall have a grade of 6% or
less.

apart. Centerline of approaches from properties on opposite sides of a public
road shall be aligned at the same point on the public roads.
(Prior Code, § 17.40.090) (Ord. 390, passed - -1993)
§ 156.179 GRADING AND DRAINAGE.
   (A)   The site shall be graded and appropriate drainage facilities installed
to remove surface run-off waters in a manner that will not affect adjacent or
nearby properties, rivers or public roads.
   (B)   Culverts, curbs, gutters, ditches, swales and other drainage
facilities shall be installed to assure that approaches, parking areas and
other traffic facilities do not obstruct drainage facilities or adversely
affect public road and traffic facilities.
   (C)   Culverts and bridges shall be large enough to accommodate potential
runoff from upstream drainage areas.
   (D)   Curbs and gutters or swales shall be required according to the
character of the area, density of development and nature of adjoining
properties and public streets.
(Prior Code, § 17.40.100) (Ord. 390, passed - -1993)
